The Ruling on Wudu in the Mosque: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Resolution
Ruling and disagreement on wudu inside the mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on wudu in the mosque, identify the basis of the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and apply the exception for wudu in a vessel.

Core Idea
Performing wudu in the mosque is generally disliked due to impurity or natural disgust, but permissible if done in a vessel — a practical Hanafi concession.

This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi dispute over the ruling of performing wudu inside the mosque. The disagreement hinges on the status of used water (maa' musta'mal): whether it is impure, pure, or simply disgusting. The later fatwa of Qadikhan provides a practical resolution by permitting wudu in a vessel, balancing reverence for the mosque with necessity.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: performing wudu in the mosque is disliked (makruh). Note the two different reasons: impurity of used water (Abu Yusuf, one narration of Abu Hanifa) and natural disgust (another narration of Abu Hanifa).
The majority view is that it is disliked, not haram.
2
Identify Imam Muhammad's opposing view
Imam Muhammad holds that used water is pure, so there is no impurity to cause dislike. Therefore, he says there is no problem (la ba'sa bihi) with wudu in the mosque.
Muhammad's position is based on his opinion that used water is pure and purifying.
3
Examine the alternative basis from Abu Hanifa
Even according to the narration where Abu Hanifa considers used water pure, he still rules it disliked due to natural disgust (istighrar tab'i). The mosque must be kept free from such disgusting matter, just as it is kept free from mucus and phlegm.
This shows that the dislike can be independent of impurity.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
On Muhammad's view, wudu in the mosque is always permissible. On the majority view, it is generally disliked except when done in a vessel. The practical difference is whether one can perform wudu in the mosque without a container.
The thamarah determines actual practice in the mosque.
5
Apply the resolution from Qadikhan's fatwa
Qadikhan rules that performing wudu in a vessel (ina') inside the mosque is permissible (ja'iz) according to all. This reconciles the dispute by allowing wudu that does not cause direct contact with the mosque floor or walls.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البدائع ويكره التوضؤ في المسجد عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد لا بأس به لأنه عنده طاهر، وأما أبو يوسف فلأنه يقول بنجاسته، وكذا ما روي عن أبي حنيفة . وأما على رواية الطهارة عنه فلأنه مستقذر طبعاً فيجب تنزيه المسجد عنه كما يجب تنزيهه عن المخاط والبلغم ا هـ . وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : وإن توضأ في إناء في المسجد جاز عندهم.
And in al-Badai'i: It is disliked to perform wudu in the mosque according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said there is no problem because it is pure in his view. As for Abu Yusuf, it is because he considers it impure, and similarly that which is narrated from Abu Hanifa. As for the narration of purity from him, it is because it is naturally disgusting, so the mosque must be kept free from it just as it must be kept free from mucus and phlegm, end. And in the Fatawa of Qadikhan: If one performs wudu in a vessel in the mosque, it is permissible according to them.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage records an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling (hukm) of performing wudu inside a mosque. The central issue is the status of used water (maa' musta'mal). According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, used water is impure (najis), so performing wudu in the mosque would introduce impurity into a sacred place, making it disliked (makruh). According to Imam Muhammad, used water is pure (tahir), so there is no objection. However, according to another narration from Abu Hanifa maintaining purity, the dislike remains due to natural disgust (istighrar tab'i), similar to phlegm, necessitating the mosque's sanctity. The later fatwa from Qadikhan permits wudu if performed in a vessel within the mosque, suggesting a practical concession. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position likely permits wudu in a vessel, as it balances the sanctity of the mosque and practical need.

Key Terms
التوضؤ في المسجد (al-tawaddu' fi al-masjid): Performing the ritual washing (wudu) inside a mosque, as opposed to outside or in a designated area.
ماء مستعمل (maa' musta'mal): Water that has already been used for ritual purification (wudu or ghusl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is disliked (makruh).
B) It is permissible (ja'iz).
C) It is prohibited (haram).
D) It is obligatory (wajib).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits wudu in a mosque if done in a vessel, resolving an internal dispute over the status of used water and the sanctity of the mosque.

The Hanafi Ruling on Used Water: Pure but Not Purifying
Determination that used water is not purifying and the inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on used water, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Used water is pure but cannot purify—a fine distinction that determines its legal use.

Water used for wudu or ghusl enters a special category in Hanafi fiqh: it is not impure, but it is also not purifying. This ruling, confirmed in the zahir al-riwayah, raises important questions about what we can do with it. In this lesson, we will explore the evidence, the internal debates among Hanafi imams, and the major disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Locate the passage that states how used water is classified—pure but not purifying—and note the restriction to hadath vs. najasah.
The ruling distinguishes between removing ritual impurity (hadath) and physical impurity (najasah).
2
Map the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding used water's purity and its ability to remove najasah.
Muhammad holds it is pure, but still cannot remove najasah because only absolute water suffices.
3
Analyse the Hanafi dalil
Examine the proof from the practice of the Prophet and companions: they did not collect used water during travels despite needing water.
The absence of collection indicates the water was not considered suitable for reuse in purification.
4
Understand the opposing school's argument
The Shafi'i school and others cite the Quranic verse 'water tahur' (al-Furqan: 48) and argue that used water is still absolute water.
They interpret 'tahur' as meaning purifying others, while Hanafis interpret it as pure in itself.
5
Derive the practical thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: Shafi'is allow wudu with used water; Hanafis require fresh water for wudu but permit using used water for removing najasah (per one narration).
This difference affects daily practice, especially when water is scarce.

Fourth: Regarding its ruling. Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: Our companions agreed in the apparent transmissions (zahir al-riwayah) that water used on the body does not remain purifying (tahur). End. And in al-Hidayah: It does not remove hadath (ritual impurity). The commentators said: This is its ruling, and they said it was restricted to hadath because it removes najasah (physical impurity) based on what Muhammad narrated from Abu Hanifa that used water is pure (tahir) but not purifying, because removal of actual impurity is permissible with liquids according to Abu Hanifa, as stated by al-Qawwam al-Atqani, al-Kaki in al-Mi'raj, the author of al-Nihayah, and others. However, even if used water is pure according to Muhammad, removal of actual impurity is not permissible with it in his view because in his view it is only permissible with absolute water (maa' mutlaq), and we have already stated that used water is not absolute. With this is refuted the misconception of some students of our time that used water removes najasah according to Muhammad because he says it is pure—they grasped something but missed other things. Also refuted is the misconception of some engaged in study that used water does not remove najasah by consensus because according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf it is impure so it does not remove, and even though Muhammad says it is pure, in his view only absolute water removes it as we stated, because they remembered the narration of impurity from Abu Hanifa and forgot the narration of purity from him which the verifiers (muhaqqiqun) chose and gave fatwa upon. And it is mentioned in al-Mujtaba from al-Quduri and Sharh al-Irshad and Salat al-Jalali that it is permissible to remove impurity with used water according to the apparent transmission. And what we have mentioned of its ruling with us is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and a narration of Malik. And al-Zuhri, Malik, al-Awza'i in the more famous of two narrations from them, and Abu Thawr held that it is purifying (mutahhir), and Ibn al-Mundhir chose it. They argued with His statement: 'And We sent down from the sky purifying water' (al-Furqan: 48) because 'tahur' is that which purifies others repeatedly. And the argument for our companions and those who followed them is that the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and his companions, may Allah be pleased with them, needed water in many places during their frequent travels and did not collect used water to use it again. If it is said: They did not collect because nothing would accumulate from it, the answer is that this is not conceded, and even if conceded for wudu, it is not conceded for ghusl. If it is said: Their not collecting does not necessitate prevention of purification with it, and that is why they did not collect it for drinking, cooking, kneading, cooling, and the like, the answer is that their not collecting for drinking etc. is due to disgust (istighrar), for souls naturally dislike it by habit even if it is pure, just as the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, expressed disgust at the lizard and left it: it was said: Is it forbidden? He said: No, but I dislike it. And as for purification a second time, there is no disgust in it, so their leaving it indicates its impossibility. As for the answer to their argument, it is known from what we have already stated at the beginning of the discussion that 'tahur' is not that which purifies others, let alone repeatedly. And by what we have mentioned is refuted what Sadr al-Shari'ah stated: 'We say: if it were pure, it would be permissible in travel to perform wudu with it and then drink it'—and no one said that. End. It is now known that the reason they did not drink it is disgust, not lack of purity. With.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion on the ruling of used water (maa' musta'mal). The author first establishes the consensus among Hanafi scholars in the zahir al-riwayah (apparent transmissions) that water used on the body for purification ceases to be purifying (tahur). This means it cannot be used to remove ritual impurity (hadath), though it can remove physical impurity (najasah) according to a narration from Abu Hanifa—since liquids other than water can remove najasah in his view. The passage clarifies a common misunderstanding: Imam Muhammad considers used water pure, but he still does not permit removing najasah with it because only absolute water (maa' mutlaq) qualifies for purification in his view. The text then contrasts the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i, Maliki, and other schools who consider used water purifying, citing the Quranic verse (al-Furqan: 48). The Hanafi response uses the practice of the Prophet and companions: they did not collect used water during travels, indicating it is not suitable for reuse. Arguments that they avoided it due to disgust are countered by noting that disgust would also apply to drinking but not to purification a second time. The passage concludes with a refutation of Sadr al-Shari'ah's argument and confirms that the reason for not drinking used water is disgust, not impurity. The mu'tamad (relied-upon) Hanafi position is that used water is pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr tahur), and this is the basis for fatwa.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (maa' musta'mal): Water that has been previously used for ritual purification (wudu/ghusl).
طهور (tahur): Water that is itself pure and capable of purifying others.
نجاسة حقيقية (najasah haqiqiyyah): Physical impurity (e.g., blood, urine) that can be removed by any liquid according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the status of water used for wudu?
A) It is impure (najis) and cannot be used for any purpose.
B) It is purifying (tahur) like fresh water.
C) It is pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr tahur).
D) It is purifying only for removing physical impurity, not ritual impurity.

Key Takeaway
Used water is legally pure but cannot be used for ritual purification; this ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet and refined by Hanafi usul.

The Well Issue (Juhut): The Three Hanafi Positions on a Junub's Immersion
Complete matrix of rulings for a junub entering a well

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the well issue, explain the reasoning of each imam, and identify the practical consequence of the difference.

Core Idea
The three letters of juhut encode the entire intra-Hanafi dispute on a junub's immersion: najis, unchanging, and pure.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute known as the 'well issue' (mas'alah al-bi'r), memorably summarized by the acronym 'juhut' (جحط). The scenario is deceptively simple: a person in a state of major impurity (junub) submerges in a well. Yet the three great Hanafi imams — Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani — each derive a different ruling on the purity of both the person and the water. Understanding these divergent rulings and their underlying reasons is essential for mastering Hanafi usul al-fiqh and the concept of ikhtilaf within the school.

Guided Path
1
Decode the Acronym
Understand that juhut stands for the three positions: Jim (ج) = najis (both impure), Ha (ح) = hal (both unchanged), Ta (ط) = tahir (both pure).
The letters are arranged in order of the imams: first Abu Hanifa, second Abu Yusuf, third Muhammad.
2
Identify the Disputed Element
Recognize that the dispute centers on the conditions necessary for the obligation (fard) of ghusl to be fulfilled when a junub immerses in well water: specifically, the role of intention (niyyah) and pouring (sabb).
Abu Hanifa does not require intention; Abu Yusuf requires pouring; Muhammad does not require pouring.
3
Follow Each Imam's Reasoning
Trace how each imam applies his conditions to reach his ruling: Abu Hanifa: first contact fulfills obligation, making water used and impure, man remains junub; Abu Yusuf: no pouring means obligation not fulfilled, man remains junub, water unchanged; Muhammad: pouring not required, obligation fulfilled, man pure, water pure.
Qadikhan's fatwa clarifies that on Abu Hanifa's view, the man emerges from janabah first via complete submersion, then water becomes impure.
4
Analyze the Practical Difference (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Consider the scenario of rinsing the mouth after exiting the well. According to Abu Hanifa's apparent view, the man is still junub and cannot recite Quran; according to Abu Yusuf, also cannot; according to Muhammad, he can. Qadikhan's tarjih allows recitation on Abu Hanifa's view after rinsing.
The practical effect is the permissibility of reciting Quran and entering the mosque.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
Note that Qadikhan states the most apparent view (azhar) is that on Abu Hanifa's position, the man becomes pure first via complete submersion, then the water becomes impure. Thus, after rinsing, he may recite Quran. This shows how later Hanafi masters resolve practical applications.
Other narrations and refinements exist; the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view as clarified by Qadikhan.

قوله: (ومسألة البئر جحط أي ضابط حكم مسألة البئر جحط وصورتها: جنب انغمس في البئر للدلو أو للتبرد ولا نجاسة على بدنه فعند أبي حنيفة الرجل والماء نجسان، وعند أبي يوسف الرجل جنب على حاله والماء مطهر على حاله وعند محمد الرجل طاهر والماء طاهر طهور، فالجيم من النجس علامة نجاستهما والحاء من الحال أي كلاهما بحاله، والطاء من الطاهر فرتب حروفه على ترتيب الأئمة. فالحرف الأوّل للإمام الأعظم، والثاني للثاني والثالث للثالث وجه قول أبي حنيفة أن الفرض قد سقط عن بعض الأعضاء بأول الملاقاة لأن النية ليست بشرط لسقوط الفرض فإذا سقط الفرض صار الماء مستعملاً عنده فيتنجس الماء، والرجل باقٍ على جنابته لبقاء الحدث في أنه يخرج من الجنابة ثم يتنجس بالماء النجس حتى لو تمضمض واستنشق حل له قراءة القرآن ا هـ. ووجه قول أبي يوسف أن الصب شرط لاسقاط الفرض عنده في غير الماء الجاري وما هو في حكمه ولم يوجد فكان الرجل جنباً بحاله فإذا لم يسقط الفرض ولم يوجد رفع الحدث ولا نية القربة لا يصير الماء مستعملاً فكان بحاله . ووجه قول محمد على ما هو الصحيح عنه أن الصب ليس بشرط عنده فكان الرجل طاهراً ولا الماء مستعملاً وإن يصير أزيل به حدث للضرورة، وإما على ما خرجه أبو بكر الرازي فإنه لا الماء مستعملاً عنده يصير ذلك عن أبي على قاضيخان وقيد بقوله في إناء» لأنه لو كان في غير إناء فهو على الخلاف المتقدم والله تعالى اعلم اهـ. قول المصنف : ومسألة البئر (جحط قال في النهر : وروي نحط بالنون روي كما في غاية البيان قوله : (وقيل عنده الخ) هذا مبني على أن الماء لا يعطى له حكم الاستعمال بأول الملاقاة، ويدل على ذلك عبارة الخانية فإنها تفيد أن نجس الماء بالاستعمال بعد الخروج من الجنابة، وذلك بتمام الانغماس وإلا لزم بقاء الجنابة. ثم الظاهر أن الرجل على القول الأول نجس بكل من نجاسة الجنابة ونجاسة الماء لملاقاة بقية جسده الماء الهداية على ذكر طلب الدلو .
His statement: 'And the well issue (juhut)', i.e., the summary rule for the well issue is juhut. Its scenario: A junub (person in major impurity) submerges in a well to fetch a bucket or to cool off, and there is no impurity on his body. According to Abu Hanifa: both the man and the water are impure (najis). According to Abu Yusuf: the man remains junub as he was, and the water remains purifying as it was. According to Muhammad: the man is pure (tahir) and the water is pure and purifying (tahir tahur). The letter jim is from najis, indicating their impurity; ha is from hal (state), meaning both remain in their state; ta is from tahir. So the letters are arranged according to the order of the imams: the first letter for the Great Imam (Abu Hanifa), the second for the second (Abu Yusuf), and the third for the third (Muhammad). The reasoning for Abu Hanifa's view: The obligation (fard) has been fulfilled from some limbs at the first contact because intention is not a condition for completing the obligation. Once the obligation is fulfilled, the water becomes used water in his view, so the water becomes impure, and the man remains in his state of janabah because hadath remains on the other limbs. It is also said that in his view, the man becomes impure due to the impurity of the used water. In the commentaries of al-Hidayah, it is verified that he is impure due to janabah in his view. The benefit of the difference appears in reciting the Quran and entering the mosque if he rinses and sniffs water. In the Fatawa of Qadikhan, the most apparent is that he emerges from janabah then becomes impure with the impure water, so if he rinses and sniffs, it becomes permissible for him to recite the Quran, end. The reasoning for Abu Yusuf's view: Pouring (sabb) is a condition for completing the obligation in his view for non-running water and its equivalent, and this (pouring) did not occur, so the man remains junub as he was. Since the obligation is not completed and neither removal of hadath nor intention of worship occurred, the water does not become used, so it remains as it was. The reasoning for Muhammad's view, according to what is correct from him: Pouring is not a condition in his view, so the man becomes pure, and neither does the water become used; rather, it is removed by necessity (darurah). Alternatively, according to what Abu Bakr al-Razi extracted: used water does not become (?) in his view. That is from the statement of Qadikhan, and he restricted it with the phrase 'in a vessel' because if it were not in a vessel, it follows the earlier disagreement. And Allah knows best, end. The author's statement: 'And the well issue (juhut)'. It is said in al-Nahr: and it is also narrated as 'nuhut' with nun, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. His statement: ('It is said in his view...') is built on the principle that water is not given the ruling of use at the first contact. This is supported by the expression in al-Khaniyah which indicates that the water becomes impure through use after emerging from janabah, and that is by complete submersion; otherwise, janabah would remain. Then it is apparent that on the first view, the man is impure from both janabah and the impurity of the water due to the rest of his body contacting water that is ruled impure at first contact. Consider. His statement: ('due to necessity') is inconsistent with what he first mentioned in the issue: 'or to cool off,' because there is no necessity there, unlike submersion to retrieve a bucket. Carefully consider. That is why al-Hidayah confined itself to mentioning seeking the bucket.

Commentary
This passage presents the classic Hanafi 'well issue' (mas'alah al-bi'r), summarized by the acronym 'juhut' (جحط). The scenario: a person in a state of major impurity (junub) immerses himself in a well, either to retrieve a lost bucket or to cool off, with no physical impurity on his body. The three Hanafi imams give different rulings: Abu Hanifa (first letter: jim) rules that both the man and the water become impure (najis). His reasoning: the first contact with water partially fulfills the obligation of ghusl (since intention is not required), making the water considered 'used water' and thus impure; the man remains junub due to the remaining body parts not yet washed. Abu Yusuf (second letter: ha) holds that the man remains junub and the water remains purifying as before. His reasoning: pouring (sabb) is a condition for the obligation to be lifted; since he immersed without pouring, the obligation is not fulfilled, so the water does not become used. Muhammad (third letter: ta) holds that both are pure (tahir), and the water is even purifying (tahur). His reasoning: pouring is not a condition; the obligation is fulfilled, making the man pure. The water does not become used (or if used, it removes the hadath by necessity). The practical benefit (fai'dah) of this difference appears when the person rinses his mouth and nose after exiting: on Abu Hanifa's view, he remains junub and cannot recite Quran or enter mosque; on the other views, he can. Qadikhan's fatwa clarifies that in Abu Hanifa's school, the man actually emerges from janabah first (by complete submersion) and then the water becomes impure, so rinsing does permit Quran recitation. The passage also discusses alternative narrations and the condition of necessity (darurah) for Muhammad's view, noting that al-Hidayah only mentions fetching a bucket, not cooling off, because cooling off has no necessity. The terminology 'juhut' is a helpful mnemonic: ج = نجس (najis), ح = حال (unchanged), ط = طاهر (pure).

Key Terms
جحط (juhut): An acronym summarizing the three Hanafi rulings on the well issue: Jim (Abu Hanifa: both impure), Ha (Abu Yusuf: both unchanged), Ta (Muhammad: both pure).
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl (e.g., after sexual intercourse or menstruation).
صب (sabb): Pouring water over oneself during ghusl; a condition for completing ghusl in Abu Yusuf's view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the well issue (juhut), what does the letter 'ha' (ح) stand for?
A) نجس (impure)
B) حال (state unchanged)
C) طاهر (pure)
D) حلال (permissible)

Key Takeaway
The juhut acronym captures the three intra-Hanafi positions on a junub's immersion: Abu Hanifa (both impure), Abu Yusuf (both unchanged), Muhammad (both pure) – a foundational lesson in ikhtilaf and practical fiqh.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Well Water Issue: Three Hanafi Positions on the Junub Immersing in a Well
Explains the three Hanafi positions using the acronym جحط and the mufta bihi via talfiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the well issue and explain the relied-upon mufta bihi position derived through talfiq.

Core Idea
The relied-upon Hanafi position on the well issue combines Abu Hanifa's view on the man's purity with Muhammad's view on the water's purity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a classic Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute: what is the ruling when a person in a state of janaba fully immerses in a well to retrieve a bucket or cool off, without any physical impurity? The text presents three distinct positions from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, then explains why all three are weak and how the mufta bihi position is derived by combining elements of two of them. Understanding this issue is essential for grasping how later Hanafi jurists practice talfiq (combining narrations) to arrive at a practical fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The issue involves a junub (person in major ritual impurity) who fully immerses in a well without any physical impurity on his body, either to retrieve a bucket or to cool down.
No bodily impurities (najasa) are present; only ritual impurity (hadath akbar).
2
Memorize the acronym جحط
The acronym جحط (j-h-t) summarizes the three positions: J = najis (impure), H = hal (state, i.e., unchanged), T = tahir (pure). The letters correspond to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad respectively.
Arrange: first letter for Abu Hanifa, second for Abu Yusuf, third for Muhammad.
3
Distinguish the three positions
Abu Hanifa: both man and water become impure. Abu Yusuf: man remains junub, water remains purifying. Muhammad: man becomes pure, water remains pure and purifying.
These are the original positions before talfiq.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each
Abu Hanifa: the first contact removes the obligation of ghusl from some limbs, making the water musta'mal (used) and thus impure; the man remains junub for the rest. Abu Yusuf: pouring (sabb) is a condition for removal, absent here, so no change. Muhammad: pouring is not a condition; necessity prevents the water from becoming used.
The reasoning is talil (causal explanation).
5
Understand the mufta bihi via talfiq
All three original positions are considered weak. The mufta bihi combines Abu Hanifa's narration that the man becomes pure (water does not become used before separation) with Muhammad's view that used water is pure but not purifying (tahir ghair tahur). Thus: man is pure, water is pure but not purifying.
This combination is called talfiq, permissible within the Hanafi school.

ذلك عبارة الخانية فإنها تفيد أن نجس الماء بالاستعمال بعد الخروج من الجنابة، وذلك بتمام الانغماس وإلا لزم بقاء الجنابة. ثم الظاهر أن الرجل على القول الأول نجس بكل من نجاسة الجنابة ونجاسة الماء لملاقاة ولذا اقتصر في الهداية على ذكر طلب الدلو . ١٧٦ كتاب الطهارة كما توجب لفقد نية القربة وهي شرط عنده في صيرورته مستعملاً، وهذه المسألة أخذ منها أبو بكر الرازي الاختلاف في سبب استعمال الماء بين الأصحاب، وقد تقدم أن أخذه منها غير لازم ذكره شمس الأئمة . وقال الخبازي في حاشية الهداية قال القدوري رحمه الله : كان شيخنا أبو عبد الله الجرجاني يقول : الصحيح عندي من مذهب أصحابنا أن إزالة الحدث استعمال الماء ولا معنى لهذا الخلاف إذ لا نص فيه. وإنما لم يأخذ حكم الاستعمال في مسألة طلب الدلو لمكان الضرورة إذا لحاجة إلى الانغماس في البئر لطلب الدلو مما يتكرر، فلو احتاجوا إلى الغسل عند نزح ماء البئر كل مرة لحرجوا حرجاً عظيماً وصار كالمحدث إذا اغترف الماء بكفه لا يصير مستعملاً بلا خلاف وإن وجد إسقاط الفرض لمكان الضرورة بخلاف ما إذا أدخل غير اليد فيه صار الماء مستعملاً ا.هـ. وعن أبي حنيفة أن الرجل طاهر لأن الماء لا يعطي له حكم الاستعمال قبل الانفصال من العضو. وقال الزيلعي والهندي وغيرهما تبعاً لصاحب الهداية : وهذه الرواية أوفق الروايات أي للقياس، وفي فتح القدير وشرح المجمع أنها الرواية المصححة ا هـ. وتعليلهم هذا يفيد أنه لو تمضمض واستنشق داخل البئر قبل انفصاله لا يخرج عن الجنابة لصيرورة الماء مستعملاً قبل الانفصال، وقد صرح به في السراج الوهاج فعلم بما قررناه أن المذهب المختار في هذه المسألة أن الرجل طاهر والماء طاهر غير طهور. أما كون الرجل طاهراً على الصحيح فقد علمته. وأما كون الماء مستعملاً كذلك على الصحيح فقد علمته أيضاً مما قدمناه قوله : (فعلم بما قررناه (الخ) قال سيدي العارف بالله عبد الغني في شرح الهدية : والحاصل أن هذه المسألة مسألة البئر «جحط) الأقوال الثلاثة فيها ضعيفة لأن القولين الأولين مبنيان على نجاسة الماء المستعمل، أما على قول الإمام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله فظاهر، وأما على قول أبي يوسف فالذي منع من الحكم بنجاسة الماء عدم وجود الصب عنده فلو وجد الحكم بالنجاسة ونجاسة المستعمل واشتراط الصب قولان ضعيفان والقول الثالث وهو قول محمد رحمه الله مبني على طهارة الماء المستعمل واشتراط نية القربة له. أما طهارة المستعمل فقد ذكرنا فيما سبق أن ذلك هو الصحيح المفتى به، وأما اشتراط نية القربة له فغير مأخوذ به لتصريحهم بأن الماء يصير مستعملاً بكل من رفع الحدث والقربة وإسقاط الفرض كما سبق بيانه فيكون المفتى به على قول محمد طهارة الماء المستعمل فقط لاشتراط نية القربة ولكن فيه تلفيق في التقليد، ولعل ذلك لا يضر لأن أقوال الصحب روايات عن أبي حنيفة كما هو المشهور والكل مذهبه فيصير الماء مستعملاً على هذا وإن لم ينو القربة وهو طاهر غير طهور اهـ. والتلفيق إنما هو في قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد حيث أخذ بما روي عنه أن الرجل طاهر، وبرواية محمد عنه أن المستعمل طاهر غير طهور ولم يؤخذ بقوله أنه مستعمل وهو نجس، ولا بقول محمد أنه غير مستعمل وبه ظهر وجه قول الشارح أن الرجل طاهر والماء طاهر غير طهور. قوله: (والماء طاهر
Book of Purity. ... The issue of the well (j-h-t): a junub immerses in a well to fetch a bucket or to cool off, with no impurity on his body. According to Abu Hanifa: both the man and the water are impure. According to Abu Yusuf: the man remains junub, the water remains purifying. According to Muhammad: the man is pure and the water is pure and purifying. The letter jim stands for impure (najis), ha for the state (hal), ta for pure (tahir), arranged according to the order of the imams. The proof of Abu Hanifa: the obligation (of ghusl) has been removed from some limbs by the first contact because intention is not a condition; thus the water becomes used and impure, while the man remains in janaba due to the remaining parts. The proof of Abu Yusuf: pouring is a condition for removal of obligation in non-flowing water; since it is absent, the man remains junub and the water does not become used. The proof of Muhammad: pouring is not a condition; the man becomes pure and the water does not become used due to necessity. ... The chosen madhhab is that the man is pure and the water is pure but not purifying. The three opinions are all weak. The fatwa position combines elements of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's views such that the water is considered used (musta'mal) and pure but not purifying.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the well-known issue of a junub person fully immersing in a well. The author presents the three Hanafi positions using the acronym 'j-h-t' (جحط). The scenario is: a person in a state of major ritual impurity (janaba) immerses himself in a well in order to retrieve a bucket or to cool down, and there is no physical impurity (najasa) on his body. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, both the man and the water become impure (najis). According to Abu Yusuf, the man remains junub and the water remains purifying (mutahhir). According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, both the man and the water are pure and the water remains purifying (tahur). The author explains the reasoning behind each position. Abu Hanifa argues that the first contact with water removes the obligation of ghusl from the parts that have been wetted, and since intention is not a condition for removal, the water becomes used (musta'mal) and therefore impure. The man remains junub because the remaining body parts still need ghusl. Abu Yusuf requires pouring (sabb) for the removal of obligation in non-flowing water; since the immersion does not involve pouring, the water does not become used. Muhammad holds that pouring is not a condition and also considers the necessity of the situation (e.g., retrieving the bucket), so the water does not become used and the man becomes pure. The passage then cites various authorities and concludes that the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the man is pure and the water is pure but not purifying (tahir ghair tahur). This is achieved by combining Abu Hanifa's view about the man being pure (from one narration) and Muhammad's view that used water is pure but not purifying. The three original positions are considered weak because they rely on problematic assumptions about used water. The commentary emphasizes that the practical ruling for fatwa is the 'talfiq' (combination) of these views.

Key Terms
جحط (j-h-t / JahT): Acronym summarizing three Hanafi positions on the well issue: Jim for najis, Ha for hal, Ta for tahir.
مستعمل (musta'mal): Water that has been used to remove ritual impurity (hadath) and is no longer purifying; considered impure or pure depending on the view.
تلفيق (talfiq): Combination of different narrations or opinions to arrive at the operative fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the well issue (مسألة البئر), what is the status of a junub who immerses to retrieve a bucket?
A) The man is junub and the water is impure.
B) The man is pure and the water remains purifying.
C) The man is pure and the water is pure but not purifying.
D) The man is junub and the water is purifying.

Key Takeaway
In the well issue, the mufta bihi Hanafi position is that the man is pure and the water is pure but not purifying, achieved by combining Abu Hanifa's narration on the man's purity with Muhammad's view on used water.

The Well Case: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Used Water
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether water becomes musta'mal and the purity of the person and water in the well case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three intra-Hanafi positions on the well case and explain the relied-upon talfiq position.

Core Idea
When a junub descends into a well, the man becomes pure but the water becomes musta'mal (pure, not purifying).

Imagine a man in a state of janabah who must enter a well to retrieve a bucket. Does his immersion in the water remove his impurity? Does the water become unusable? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a famous intra-Hanafi dispute, showing how the later school combined elements from the three eponymous imams to reach a practical ruling based on necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three reports
List the three opinions from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the man's purity and the water's status.
Abu Hanifa: man pure, water musta'mal and najis. Abu Yusuf: man remains junub, water remains tahur. Muhammad: water becomes musta'mal only with intention, and is tahir ghayr tahur.
2
Understand the reasoning behind each report
For each, identify the key condition: Abu Hanifa considers water musta'mal upon contact (before separation); Abu Yusuf requires pouring (sabb); Muhammad requires intention of qurbah.
These conditions reflect different views on the cause of water becoming musta'mal.
3
Analyze the weakness of each report
The text states that the first two views are weak because they imply used water is impure, which is not the correct view. Muhammad's condition of intention is not adopted by later scholars.
The weakness is that they lead to impractical or contradictory results.
4
Recognize the talfiq and its justification
The relied-upon view combines Abu Hanifa's ruling on the man (pure) and Muhammad's ruling on the water (pure but not purifying), justified by necessity (darurah) because the well is used repeatedly.
This talfiq is accepted because all three opinions are considered narrations from Abu Hanifa.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi and its practical implication
The mufta bihi is: the man is tahir and the water is tahir ghayr tahur (musta'mal). This means the water can be used for non-purification purposes but not for wudu or ghusl.
This ruling avoids hardship while maintaining the principle that used water loses its purifying quality.

(والظاهر منه إذا نزل للدلو وتدلك في الماء صار الماء مستعملاً) أي إذا لم يكن تدلكه لإزالة الوسخ كما في البحر الرائق ج ١٢ /
Book of Purity: As it [the water] becomes musta'mal due to loss of intention of closeness, which is a condition according to him [Muhammad] for it becoming musta'mal. Abu Bakr al-Razi derived from this issue the disagreement among the companions regarding the cause of water being used. It has been mentioned that his derivation is not necessary, as stated by Shams al-A'immah. Al-Khabbazi said in his gloss on al-Hidayah: Al-Quduri said: Our teacher Abu Abdullah al-Jurjani used to say: The correct view in my opinion from the madhhab of our companions is that removal of hadath is [a form of] using water, and there is no meaning to this disagreement because there is no explicit text. The ruling of being used was not applied in the issue of seeking the bucket because of necessity, since the need to immerse in the well for the bucket recurs. If they had to perform ghusl every time they draw water from the well, they would face great hardship. Thus it becomes like a person with minor impurity who scoops water with his hand – it does not become used without dispute, even though the obligation is fulfilled due to necessity, unlike if he inserts something other than his hand, then the water becomes used. End quote. From Abu Hanifa: The man is pure because the water does not take the ruling of being used before it separates from the limb. Al-Zayla'i, al-Hindi, and others following the author of al-Hidayah said: This report is the most appropriate of the reports i.e., in analogy. In Fath al-Qadir and Sharh al-Majma', it is the corrected report. End quote. Their reasoning indicates that if he rinses his mouth and nose inside the well before it separates, he does not exit the state of janabah because the water becomes musta'mal before separation. This has been stated explicitly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. So it is known from what we have stated that the chosen madhhab in this issue is that the man is pure and the water is pure but not purifying. As for the man being pure according to the correct view, you know that. As for the water being musta'mal similarly according to the correct view, you know that from what we have presented. His statement: (So it is known from what we have stated...) Sayyidi al-Arif billah Abd al-Ghani said in his commentary on al-Hidayah: The summary is that this issue – the well issue – all three opinions are weak, because the first two opinions are based on the impurity of used water. As for the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa, it is apparent. As for the opinion of Abu Yusuf, what prevented him from ruling the water impure was the absence of pouring according to him. If pouring existed, he would rule it impure, and the impurity of used water and the condition of pouring are two weak opinions. The third opinion, that of Muhammad, is based on the purity of used water and the condition of intention of closeness. As for the purity of used water, we have mentioned previously that this is the correct and mufta bihi view. As for the condition of intention of closeness, it is not adopted because they have stated that water becomes musta'mal by both removal of hadath and closeness and by fulfilling the obligation as previously explained. Thus the mufta bihi according to Muhammad is only the purity of used water due to the condition of intention of closeness, but there is talfiq in taqlid. Perhaps that is not harmful because the statements of the companions are narrations from Abu Hanifa, as is well known, and all are his madhhab. So the water becomes musta'mal on this view even without intention of closeness, and it is pure but not purifying. End quote. The talfiq is only in the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: adopting from him the narration that the man is pure, and from Muhammad the narration that used water is pure but not purifying, not adopting his statement that it is used and impure, nor Muhammad's statement that it is not used. Thus the commentator's statement that the man is pure and the water is pure but not purifying becomes clear. His statement: (And the water is pure but not purifying) al-Ramli said: I say: It will soon come that it is pure and purifying according to the correct view. His statement: (But it is appropriate...) I say: There is consideration in this because it opposes their absolute statements of agreement. In al-Siraj it is expressed 'without dispute' and similarly with 'by agreement' except for the opinion of Zafar. What appears to me is that Abu Yusuf only stipulates pouring when he did not intend ghusl, to make pouring stand in place of intention. This is supported by what will come that if he rubs himself, it becomes musta'mal by agreement because it stands in place of intention of ghusl. His statement: (And you have known from what we have presented in the discussion on the water of cisterns...) I say: We have presented the discussion on that, so there is no need to repeat it after your comprehensiveness there. What he narrated from Ibn Amir Haj does not have strength to oppose the statement of al-Dabusi mentioned earlier, and the absolute nature of their statements that water is used by agreement. Therefore there is no need to base it on what was mentioned nor to interpret the speech contrary to its apparent meaning. Then I saw in Sharh Nazm al-Kanz by Allamah al-Maqdisi that he said: The interpretation of the speech that the intended meaning of 'it becomes musta'mal' is that what contacts his limbs from it becomes musta'mal is very far-fetched, because there is no need to explicitly state that at all. End quote. His statement: (And the apparent of it is that if he descends for the bucket and rubs himself in the water, the water becomes musta'mal) i.e., if his rubbing is not to remove dirt, as in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq volume 12.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on a junub (person in a state of major impurity) who descends into a well to retrieve a bucket (dalw) or for cooling (tabarrad). The core question is whether the water in the well becomes musta'mal (used water) and whether the person becomes pure. The text presents three positions: (1) Abu Hanifa holds that the man is pure because the water does not take the ruling of being musta'mal until it separates from the limb, but the water itself becomes musta'mal and impure (najis). (2) Abu Yusuf holds that water becomes musta'mal only with pouring (sabb), so in the well case without pouring, the water is not musta'mal and remains purifying, and the man does not become pure. (3) Muhammad ibn al-Hasan holds that water becomes musta'mal only with the intention of qurbah (seeking closeness), and the water is pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr tahur). The text then discusses the mufta bihi (relied-upon position). Citing al-Hidayah and other works, the correct view adopted by later scholars is a talfiq (combination): from Abu Hanifa, the ruling that the man is pure; from Muhammad, the ruling that the water is pure but not purifying (musta'mal). This avoids the weakness of deeming the water impure and also avoids the extreme of deeming it completely unchanged. The principle of darurah (necessity) is invoked: because immersing for the bucket is frequent, deeming the water musta'mal each time would cause hardship. The text also clarifies conditions: if a pure person descends for cooling, water does not become musta'mal; if he descends intending ghusl, water becomes musta'mal by agreement (except for Zufar's outlier opinion). Abu Yusuf's condition of pouring is considered less relevant in this necessity context. The commentary emphasizes that the relied-upon view is that the water is tahir ghayr tahur, and the man is tahir. The later author (presumably al-Ramli) notes a difference: some later texts deem the water tahur (purifying), but the correct position here is the one from al-Hidayah and others. The passage then critiques an interpretation by Ibn Amir Haj that the water only becomes musta'mal at the point of contact, deeming it far-fetched.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for removing hadath (ritual impurity) or for qurbah (seeking closeness to Allah), and is no longer purifying (ghayr tahur) but remains pure (tahir) in the preferred view.
نية القربة (niyyat al-qurbah): Intention of drawing closer to Allah through the act of purification. In this passage, it is discussed as a condition for water becoming musta'mal according to Imam Muhammad.
طاهر غير طهور (tahir ghayr tahur): Pure but not purifying. Refers to water that is ritually clean (non-najis) but cannot be used for wudu or ghusl because it has been used (musta'mal).
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah) requiring ghusl. In this mas'alah, a junub descends into the well.
صب (sabb): Pouring water over the body. According to Abu Yusuf, water becomes musta'mal only when it is poured over the limb and then separates; in the well, immersion without pouring does not make water musta'mal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) in the well case (mas'alat al-ba'ir), what is the status of the person and the water when a junub descends to retrieve a bucket?
A) The person remains junub and the water is musta'mal and impure.
B) The person becomes pure and the water is musta'mal but pure (tahir ghayr tahur).
C) The person becomes pure and the water remains purifying (tahur).
D) The person remains junub and the water remains purifying.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi ruling on the well case is a talfiq: the man becomes pure but the water becomes musta'mal (pure, not purifying), justified by necessity.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Well Water and Musta'mal: The Sound Hanafi Position
Expanding the ruling on musta'mal water and clarifying the correct Hanafi position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sound Hanafi position on well water becoming musta'mal and explain why it remains tahur based on the principle of overcoming (ghalabah).

Core Idea
Well water never becomes musta'mal because the small amount contacting the body is overcome by the bulk.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, Ibn Nujaym clarifies a common misconception about well water. While some scholars initially claimed consensus that water becomes musta'mal when a person performs ghusl in a well, the correct position from Imam Muhammad is that the entire well water remains purifying. We will trace the evidence and understand the critical distinction between the water that touches the body and the overwhelming quantity of the well.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
The text distinguishes four scenarios: a pure person immersing without intention (water does not become musta'mal), a pure person immersing with intention (becomes musta'mal), a junub immersing with intention (becomes musta'mal), and a junub immersing without intention (the dispute arises). Note that for the pure person without intention, it is agreed that water does not become musta'mal because there is no removal of hadath.
Consensus on these base cases sets the stage for the dispute on well water.
2
Extract the definition of musta'mal
The passage defines musta'mal as water that has fallen from the limbs after the removal of hadath. This definition is crucial because it implies that water must be separated from the limb to be considered musta'mal.
The definition is from the earlier discussion on fasaqi water.
3
Apply the overcoming principle
Ibn Nujaym argues that the small amount of water that contacts the limbs is 'overcome' (maghlub) by the larger quantity of the well. Since it does not separate and has no independent existence, it cannot render the entire well water musta'mal.
This is a key Hanafi istihsan argument.
4
Identify the weak and sound narrations
The passage reveals that the claim that well water becomes musta'mal is based on a weak narration from Muhammad. The sound (sahih) narration from Muhammad is that well water never becomes musta'mal.
The weak narration is from al-Mabsut; the sound narration is the chosen one.
5
Interpret the consensus statements
When scholars say 'the water became musta'mal by consensus,' they mean only the water directly contacting the body, not the entire well. This interpretation is supported by Ibn Amir Hajj and resolves the apparent contradiction.
This interpretation is contested by al-Ramli and al-Maqdisi, but Ibn Nujaym holds it.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة
قيدنا أصل المسألة بالجنب لأن الطاهر إذا انغمس لطلب الدلو ولم يكن على أعضائه نجاسة لا يصير الماء مستعملاً اتفاقاً لعدم إزالة الحدث وإقامة القربة، وإن انغمس للاغتسال صار مستعملاً اتفاقاً لوجود إقامة القربة وحكم الحدث حكم الجنابة ذكره في البدائع، وكذا حكم الحائض والنفساء إذا نزلا بعد الانقطاع، أما قبل الانقطاع وليس على أعضائهما نجاسة فإنهما كالطاهر إذا انغمس للتبرد لأنها لا تخرج من الحيض بهذا الوقوع فلا مستعملاً. كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان والخلاصة. وقيدنا بكونه انغمس لطلب الدلو أو للتبرد لأنه لو انغمس بقصد الاغتسال للصلاة قالوا صار الماء مستعملاً اتفاقاً لوجود إزالة الحدث ونية القربة لكن ينبغي أن لا يزول حدثه عند أبي يوسف لما نقلوه عنه أن الصب شرط عنده في غير الماء الجاري وما هو في حكمه لإسقاط الفرض ولم أر من صرح بهذا، وقد علمت فيما قدمناه في الكلام على ماء الفساقي أن قولهم بأن ماء البئر يصير مستعملاً عند الكل مبني على قول ضعيف عن محمد، والصحيح من مذهب محمد أن ماء البئر لا يصير مستعملاً مطلقاً لأن المستعمل هو ما تساقط عن الأعضاء وهو مغلوب بالنسبة إلى الماء الذي لم يستعمله فاحفظ هذا وكن على ذكر منه ينفعك إن شاء الله تعالى ثم رأيت بعد هذا العلامة ابن أمير حاج في شرح منية المصلي صرح بما ذكرته وقال : الماء المستعمل هو الماء الذي لاقى الرجل الذي زال حدثه فيجب نزح جميع الماء على رواية نجاسة الماء المستعمل ولا يجب نزح شيء منها على رواية طهارته بل هو باق على طهوريته وقد عرفت أن رواية الطهارة هي المختارة. فعلى هذا قولهم صار الماء مستعملاً معناه صار الماء الملاقي للبدن مستعملاً لا أن ماء البئر صار مستعملاً وقيدنا بقولنا ليس على أعضائه نجاسة حقيقية لأنه لو كان كذلك اهـ.
غير طهور) قال الرملي أقول : سيأتي قريباً أنه طاهر طهور على الصحيح. قوله : (لكن ينبغي الخ) أقول : فيه نظر لأنه مخالف لإطلاقهم الاتفاق. وعبر في السراج بقوله «بلا خلاف» وكذا بقوله بالاتفاق إلا في قول زفر والذي يظهر لي أن أبا يوسف إنما يشترط الصب فيما إذا لم ينو الاغتسال ليجعل الصب قائماً مقام النية، ويدل عليه ما سيأتي من أنه لو تدلك صار مستعملاً بالاتفاق لقيامه مقام نية الاغتسال قوله : (وقد علمت فيما قدمناه في الكلام على ماء الفساقي الخ) أقول قد قدمنا الكلام على ذلك فلا حاجة إلى الإعادة بعد إحاطتك بما هنالك، وما نقله عن ابن أمير حاج لا يقوى على معارضته كلام الدبوسي المتقدم وعلى إطلاق عباراتهم باستعمال الماء اتفاقاً، وعلى هذا فلا حاجة إلى البناء على ما ذكر ولا إلى تأويل الكلام بخلاف المتبادر منه إلى الإفهام . ثم رأيت في شرح نظم الكنز للعلامة المقدسي قال ما نصه : وأما تأويل الكلام بأن المراد بصيرورته مستعملاً صيرورة ما لاقي أعضاءه منه مستعملاً فهذا بعيد جداً إذ لا يحتاج إلى التنصيص على ذلك أصلاً اهـ. قوله: (والظاهر منه إذا نزل للدلو وتدلك في الماء صار الماء مستعملاً) أي إذا لم يكن تدلكه لإزالة الوسخ كما في البحر الرائق ج 12 /

كتاب الطهارة
أبي لتنجس الماء اتفاقاً، وقيد المسألة في المحيط بقوله لم يتدلك فيه ولم يبين مفهومه، وكذا في الخلاصة. والظاهر منه أنه إذا أنزل للدلو وتدلك في الماء صار الماء مستعملاً اتفاقاً لأن الدلك فعل منه قائم مقام نية الاغتسال فصار كما لو نزل للاغتسال. وقيد المسألة بعضهم بأن لا يكون استنجى بالأحجار، فمفهومه أنه لو كان مستنجياً بالأحجار تنجس الماء اتفاقاً لكن هذا يبتنى على أن الحجر في الاستنجاء مخفف لا مطهر وفيه خلاف ذكره في التنجيس وذكر أن المختار أنه مخفف لا مطهر وسنذكره إن شاء الله تعالى في موضعه فإن قلت: لم قال أبو يوسف بأن الصب شرط في العضو لا في الثوب؟ وما الفرق بينهما؟ قلت : روي عن أبي يوسف روايتان : في رواية أن الصب شرط فيهما ووجهه أن القياس يأبي التطهير بالغسل لأن الماء يتنجس بأول الملاقاة، وإنما حكمنا بالطهارة ضرورة أن الشرع كلفنا بالتطهير والتكليف يعتمد القدرة وسمي الماء طهوراً وذلك يقتضي حصول الطهارة به والضرورة تندفع بطريق الصب فلا ضرورة إلى طريق آخر مع أن الماء حال الصب بمنزلة ماء جار، وفي غير حالة الصب راكد والراكد أضعف من الجاري. وفي رواية أن الصب شرط في العضو لا في الثوب وهو المشهور عنه، ووجهه أن غسل الثياب بطريق الصب لا يتحقق إلا بكلفة ومشقة لأنها تغسلها النساء عادة وكل امرأة لا تجد خادماً يصب الماء عليها ولا ماء جارياً، وأما غسل البدن يتحقق بطريق الصب من غير كلفة . كذا في النهاية .
الماء مستعملاً عنده .
وقال القاضي الاسبيجابي في شرح مختصر الطحاوي : جنب اغتسل في بئر ثم إلى العشرة قال أبو يوسف : تنجس الآبار كلها. وقال محمد : يخرج من الثالثة طاهراً ثم ينظر إن كان على بدنه عين نجاسة تنجست المياه كلها وإن لم يكن عين نجاسة صارت المياه كلها مستعملة، ثم بعد الثالثة أن وجدت منه النية يصير مستعملاً، وإن لم توجد منه النية لا يصير ولو أنه غسل الثوب النجس في إجانة وعصره ثم في إجانة إلى العشرة فإن الثوب يخرج من الثالثة طاهراً والمياه الثلاثة نجسة في قولهم جميعاً، وأبو يوسف فرق بين الثوب والبدن فقال : لأن في الثوب ضرورة ولا ضرورة في البدن ا هـ . ولا يخفى أن مقتضى مذهب أبي يوسف من اشتراط الصب أن لا تتنجس المياه كلها عنده لما أن الحدث لم يزل ونية الاغتسال وإن وجدت لكن لا اعتبار بها إذا لم يصح الغسل عنده ، وقد علمت فيما قدمناه عند الكلام على ماء الفساقي أن ما ذكره الاسبيجابي وغيره من كون ماء الآبار يصير مستعملاً عند محمد مبني على القول الضعيف لا على الصحيح فارجع إليه تجد لك فرجاً كبيراً إن شاء الله تعالى. وقد ظهر لي أن قولهم بنجاسة ماء الآبار عند أبي يوسف وقولهم بنجاسة ماء البئر إذا نزل للاغتسال عنده مفرع على رواية عن أبي يوسف أن من نزل في البئر وهو جنب كان الماء نجساً والرجل نجس، وقد ذكر هذه الرواية الاسبيجابي وذكر هذه الفروع بعدها فالظاهر أنها مفرعة عليها لا على القول المشهور عنه أن الرجل بحاله والماء بحاله والله الهادي للصواب.
Book of Purification: We restricted the original issue to the junub because if a pure person immerses to fetch a bucket and has no impurity on his limbs, the water does not become musta'mal by consensus due to lack of removing hadath and performing devotion. If he immerses for ghusl, it becomes musta'mal by consensus due to performing devotion, and the ruling of hadath is like that of janabah, as mentioned in al-Bada'i. Similarly, the ruling for a menstruating woman and a woman in post-childbirth bleeding when they descend after cessation. Before cessation, if there is no impurity on their limbs, they are like a pure person immersing for cooling, because they do not exit menstruation with this immersion, so it does not become musta'mal. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Khulasa. We restricted it to his immersing for fetching a bucket or cooling, because if he immerses with the intention of ghusl for prayer, they said the water becomes musta'mal by consensus due to removing hadath and intention of devotion. But it should be that his hadath is not removed according to Abu Yusuf, as they reported from him that pouring is a condition for him in other than flowing water and what is in its ruling for dropping the obligation, and I have not seen anyone state this explicitly. And you have known from our earlier discussion on the water of fasaqi that their statement that well water becomes musta'mal by all is based on a weak narration from Muhammad. The correct from Muhammad's madhhab is that well water never becomes musta'mal, because musta'mal is what falls from the limbs, and it is overcome relative to the water that has not been used. So preserve this and keep it in mind; it will benefit you, Allah willing. Then after this I saw the scholar Ibn Amir Hajj in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli stating what I mentioned and saying: Used water is water that contacted a person whose hadath has been removed. So it is obligatory to remove all water according to the narration of impurity of used water, and no removal is required according to the narration of its purity; rather it remains on its purifying property. And you have recognized that the narration of purity is the chosen one. Accordingly, their statement 'the water became musta'mal' means the water contacting the body became musta'mal, not that the well water became musta'mal. And we restricted it by our saying 'there is no actual impurity on his limbs' because if it were otherwise (i.e., there was impurity), then [the water becomes impure by consensus]. End quote. (Not pure) Al-Ramli said: I say: It will soon come that it is pure and purifying according to the correct view. His statement: (But it should be...) I say: In this there is consideration because it contradicts their absolute statement of consensus. And he expressed in al-Siraj with 'without dispute' and likewise with 'by consensus' except for the view of Zufar. And what appears to me is that Abu Yusuf only requires pouring when he did not intend ghusl, to make pouring stand in place of intention. And it is indicated by what will come: that if he rubbed, the water becomes musta'mal by consensus because rubbing stands in place of the intention of ghusl. His statement: (And you have known from our earlier discussion on the water of fasaqi...) I say: We have already discussed that, so there is no need for repetition after your mastery of what is there. And what he narrated from Ibn Amir Hajj does not have strength to oppose the statement of al-Dabusi mentioned earlier and the absolute expressions of their using water by consensus. And accordingly, there is no need to build upon what was mentioned nor to interpret the speech contrary to what is apparent to understanding. Then I saw in Sharh Nazm al-Kanz by al-Maqdisi who said verbatim: As for interpreting the speech that by 'its becoming musta'mal' is meant the becoming musta'mal of what contacted his limbs from it, this is very far-fetched, as there is no need to specify that at all. End quote. His statement: (And the apparent is that if he descends for a bucket and rubs in the water, the water becomes musta'mal) i.e., if his rubbing is not for removing dirt, as in al-Bahr al-Raiq, vol. 12. (Page 178) Book of Purification: ...for the water to become impure by consensus. And the issue was restricted in al-Muhit by his statement 'he did not rub in it' and he did not explain its implication, and similarly in al-Khulasa. And the apparent from it is that if he descends for a bucket and rubs in the water, the water becomes musta'mal by consensus because rubbing is an action of his that stands in place of the intention of ghusl, so it becomes as if he descended for ghusl. And some restricted the issue by his not having performed istinja' with stones, so its implication is that if he had performed istinja' with stones, the water becomes impure by consensus. But this is based on the view that the stone in istinja' is lightening (mukhaffif) not purifying (mutahhir), and there is dispute about this mentioned in al-Tanjis, and it was mentioned that the chosen view is that it is lightening not purifying, and we will mention it insha'Allah in its place. If you ask: Why did Abu Yusuf say that pouring is a condition for the limb but not for the garment? And what is the difference between them? I say: Two narrations are related from Abu Yusuf: In one narration, pouring is a condition in both, and its justification is that analogy (qiyas) disallows purification by washing because the water becomes impure at the first contact. Rather, we ruled for purity due to necessity because the Law obligated us to purify, and obligation depends on ability, and water is called tahur, which implies attaining purity through it, and necessity is satisfied by the method of pouring, so there is no need for another method, especially since water during pouring is like flowing water, while without pouring it is stagnant, and stagnant is weaker than flowing. In another narration, pouring is a condition for the limb but not for the garment, and this is the well-known from him. Its justification is that washing clothes by pouring is only accomplished with hardship and difficulty because women usually wash them, and every woman does not find a servant to pour water on her nor flowing water. As for washing the body, it is accomplished by pouring without hardship. Thus in al-Nihaya. Water becomes musta'mal according to him. And al-Qadi al-Asbijabi said in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi: A junub performed ghusl in a well, then up to ten [wells]. Abu Yusuf said: All the wells become impure. Muhammad said: He emerges pure from the third, then if there is actual impurity on his body, all the waters become impure; if there is no actual impurity, all the waters become musta'mal. Then after the third, if intention is found from him, it becomes musta'mal; if intention is not found, it does not become musta'mal. And if he washed a najis garment in a basin and wrung it, then in a basin up to ten, the garment emerges pure from the third, and the three waters are impure according to all of them. And Abu Yusuf differentiated between the garment and the body, saying: Because in the garment there is necessity, and there is no necessity in the body. End quote. And it is not hidden that the implication of Abu Yusuf's madhhab of requiring pouring is that all the waters do not become impure according to him, because hadath has not been removed and even if intention of ghusl existed, it is not considered if ghusl is not valid according to him. And you have known from our earlier discussion on the water of fasaqi that what al-Asbijabi and others mentioned that well water becomes musta'mal according to Muhammad is based on the weak narration, not the correct one. So refer to it, you will find a great relief for you, insha'Allah. And it has appeared to me that their statement of impurity of well water according to Abu Yusuf and their statement of impurity of well water if he descended for ghusl according to him are branches of a narration from Abu Yusuf that whoever descends into a well while junub, the water is impure and the man is impure. Al-Asbijabi mentioned this narration and mentioned these branches after it, so the apparent is that they are branches of it, not of his well-known statement that the man is in his state and the water is in its state. And Allah is the Guide to the correct.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion probe on the ruling of water becoming musta'mal (used) when a person enters a well or body of water. The author, Ibn Nujaym, is commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. He begins by restricting the discussion to the case of a junub (one in major ritual impurity) because for a pure person (tahir) who immerses to fetch a bucket without any impurity on his limbs, the water does not become musta'mal by consensus (ittifaqan) since there is no removal of hadath or performance of devotion (qurbah). However, if the pure person immerses with the intention of ghusl (full ablution), the water becomes musta'mal by consensus because the intention and act of devotion are present. The same ruling applies to a menstruating woman or a woman in postpartum bleeding if they descend after the bleeding has stopped; before cessation, they are like a pure person immersing for cooling, as they do not exit their state of ritual impurity through mere immersion. This is cited from Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Khulasa.

The author then addresses a nuance: if a person immerses with the intention of ghusl for prayer, the water becomes musta'mal by consensus due to the removal of hadath and intention of devotion. However, he notes that according to Abu Yusuf, the hadath should not be removed because Abu Yusuf stipulates that pouring (sabb) is a condition for removing hadath in still water (non-flowing). The author observes that he has not seen anyone explicitly state this implication. He then refers to an earlier discussion on the water of fasaqi (public water dispensaries) to clarify that the statement that well water becomes musta'mal by everyone is based on a weak narration from Muhammad (al-Shaybani). The sound (sahih) position of Muhammad is that well water never becomes musta'mal because musta'mal is defined as water that has fallen from the limbs after washing, and the water in the well is in such a large quantity that the small amount that contacts the limbs is overcome (maghlub) by the rest. Thus, the well water remains tahur (purifying). The author urges the reader to remember this.

He then quotes Ibn Amir Hajj from his commentary on Munyat al-Musalli, who explicitly states that used water is water that has contacted a person whose hadath has been removed. According to the narration that used water is impure (najis), all the water must be removed; according to the narration that it is pure (tahir), no removal is required and it remains purifying. The chosen (mukhtar) view is the narration of purity. Therefore, when scholars say 'the water became musta'mal,' they mean only the water that directly contacted the body, not the entire well water. The condition that there be no actual impurity (najasah haqiqiyyah) on the limbs is added because if there is, the water becomes impure by consensus.

Al-Ramli objects to Ibn Nujaym's earlier comment that Abu Yusuf's condition of pouring might prevent the removal of hadath, arguing that it contradicts the explicit consensus statements. He notes that in al-Siraj and other works, the ruling is stated as 'without dispute' except for Zufar. Al-Ramli explains that Abu Yusuf only requires pouring when the person did not intend ghusl, making the pouring stand in place of intention. This is supported by the fact that if a person rubs (tadallaka) his body while in the water, the water becomes musta'mal by consensus because rubbing acts like the intention of ghusl. Thus, the earlier concern about Abu Yusuf's condition is unnecessary.

The author then cites al-Maqdisi's commentary on Nazm al-Kanz, who strongly rejects the interpretation that 'becoming musta'mal' refers only to the water in contact with the limbs, saying such an interpretation is far-fetched and unnecessary.

Further, the author discusses the scenario of a person descending for a bucket and rubbing (tadalluka) in the water. According to al-Muhit and al-Khulasa, the ruling is not explicit about rubbing, but the apparent view is that it makes the water musta'mal by consensus because rubbing is equivalent to the intention of ghusl. Some scholars added a condition: that the person must not have performed istinja' (cleaning after relieving oneself) using stones, because if he did, the water would become impure by consensus. This is based on the view that stones are only lightening (mukhaffif) not purifying (mutahhir). The author notes that this will be discussed in its proper place.

A question arises: why did Abu Yusuf say pouring is a condition for the limb but not for the garment? The author explains that there are two narrations from Abu Yusuf: one that pouring is a condition for both, and the other (and more famous) that it is a condition only for the limb. The first narration is based on qiyas (analogy): water becomes impure upon first contact, but purification is a legal obligation that must be possible, so pouring overcomes the weakness of stagnant water. The second narration is based on practical difference: washing garments by pouring is burdensome for women, who typically do the laundry without assistance, while washing the body by pouring is not burdensome.

Finally, the author presents a scenario from al-Asbijabi's commentary: If a junub performs ghusl in a well and then continues to ten wells, Abu Yusuf says all wells become impure. Muhammad says the person emerges pure from the third well; if there is actual impurity on his body, all waters become impure; if no actual impurity, all waters become musta'mal. After the third well, if intention is present, the water becomes musta'mal; otherwise not. In contrast, when washing a najis garment in basins, all agree the garment becomes pure after three washings, but the three waters are impure. Abu Yusuf distinguishes between garment (necessity) and body (no necessity). The author concludes that this ruling of impurity at Abu Yusuf is based on a weak narration and not his well-known position. The correct position is that the man and the water each remain in their original state (i.e., the water remains pure). The guidance is from Allah.

Key Terms
مستعمل (musta'mal): Water that has been used for purification and has fallen from the limbs. In this passage, it is debated whether well water can become musta'mal.
طهور (tahur): Water that is pure and purifying. Well water retains this status according to the sound position.
مغلوب (maghlub): Overcome; the small amount of water contacting the limbs is considered overcome by the larger quantity of the well, so it does not affect the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the sound Hanafi position (Muhammad's saheeh narration), what is the ruling on well water after a junub performs ghusl in it without any actual impurity?
A) The entire well water becomes musta'mal and cannot be used.
B) The water becomes impure and must be removed.
C) The water remains tahur and can be used for purification.
D) The water becomes musta'mal but is still pure.

Key Takeaway
Well water remains tahur even after ghusl performed in it, as the contacting water is overcome by the bulk and does not render the entire well musta'mal.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Rubbing, Pouring, and Multiple Wells: Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Expanding on the intra-Hanafi disputes regarding conditions for water becoming musta'mal in wells.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions of rubbing (dalk) and pouring (sabb) to determine the status of well water and evaluate the different opinions within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Rubbing in water is equivalent to intention for ghusl; Abu Yusuf's requirement of pouring applies only when there is no intention.

The previous lesson established the sound position that well water remains tahur. However, several nuanced situations arise: when a person rubs in the water, when he has performed istinja' with stones, and when multiple wells are involved. Moreover, Abu Yusuf's condition of pouring (sabb) introduces further complexity. This lesson unpacks these intra-Hanafi disputes and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Understand the effect of rubbing (dalk)
The text states that if a person descends to fetch a bucket and rubs his body in the water, the water becomes musta'mal by consensus (provided the rubbing is not for removing dirt). This is because rubbing substitutes for the intention of ghusl.
This ruling assumes the person did not originally intend ghusl; the rubbing changes the ruling.
2
Examine the condition of istinja' with stones
Some scholars restrict the previous ruling to cases where the person did not perform istinja' with stones. If he did, the water becomes impure (najis) due to the stone being only lightening, not purifying. This is based on a specific view that will be elaborated later.
This shows how the ruling branches on a subsidiary issue.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's condition of pouring (sabb)
Abu Yusuf holds that in still water, pouring is a condition for the removal of hadath. If a person immerses without pouring, his hadath is not removed, and therefore the water does not become musta'mal (or becomes impure in one narration). The passage mentions two narrations from Abu Yusuf: one requiring sabb for both limb and garment, and the famous one requiring it only for the limb.
The difference between limb and garment is based on necessity (hardship).
4
Apply the multiple well scenario
Al-Asbijabi's scenario: if a junub performs ghusl in a well and then in a series of wells, Abu Yusuf says all become impure; Muhammad says he emerges pure from the third well, and subsequent wells become musta'mal if intention is present. This shows the clash of principles.
Muhammad's view here is based on the weak narration; the sound position avoids these complications entirely.
5
Trace the weak narration and its consequences
The passage concludes that the rulings of impurity at Abu Yusuf are based on a weak narration not his famous position. The sound view is that the well water remains as it was. This reinforces the earlier lesson.
Understanding the hierarchy of narrations is essential for correct fatwa.
