⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة بيع بالدباغ. وقال في باب الحدث وجلد الكلب يطهر عندنا بالدباغ خلافاً للحسن والشافعي لأن عينه نجس عندهما ولكننا نقول : الانتفاع به مباح الاختيار فلو كان عينه نجسة لما أبيح الانتفاع به، وهذا صريح في مخالفة الأول. وذكر أيضاً في كتاب الصيد في مسألة الكلب في التعليل قال : وبهذا يتبين أنه ليس بنجس العين. وذكر في الإيضاح اختلاف الرواية فيه . وفي مبسوط شيخ الإسلام وأما جلد الكلب فعن أصحابنا فيه روايتان في رواية يظهر بالدبغ وفي رواية لا يطهر وهو الظاهر من المذهب. وذكر في البدائع أن فيه اختلاف المشايخ فمن قال إنه نجس العين جعله كالخنزير، ومن جعله طاهر العين جعله مثل سائر الحيوانات سوى الخنزير، والصحيح أنه ليس بنجس العين وكذا صححه في موضع آخر وقال : إنه أقرب القولين إلى الصواب ولذلك قال مشايخنا فيمن صلى وفي كمه جرو إنه تجوز صلاته وقيد الفقيه أبو جعفر الهندواني الجواز بكونه مشدود الفم هـ. ولذا صحح في الهداية طهارة عينه وتبعه شارحوها كالأتقاني والكاكي والسغناقي، واختار قاضيخان في الفتاوى نجاسة عينه وفرع عليها فروعاً فالحاصل أنه قد اختلف التصحيح فيه والذي يقتضيه عموم ما في المتون كالقدوري والمختار والكنز طهارة عينه ولم يعارضه ما يوجب نجاستها فوجب أحقية تصحيح عدم نجاستها، ألا ترى أنه ينتفع به حراسة واصطياداً. وقد صرح في عقد الفوائد شرح منظومة ابن وهبان بأن الفتوى على طهارة عينه، وأما ما استدل به في المبسوط من قول محمد وليس الميت بأنجس من الكلب والخنزير فقد قال في غاية البيان لا نسلم أن نجاسة العين تثبت في الكلب بهذا القدر من الكلام، فمن ادعى ذلك فعليه البيان ولم يرد نص عن محمد في نجاسة العين، وما أورده من أنه لا يلزم من الانتفاع به طهارة عينه فإن السرقين ينتفع به إيقاداً وتقوية للزراعة مع نجاسة عينه. أجاب عنه في النهاية وغيرها بأن هذا الانتفاع بالاستهلاك وهو جائز في نجس العين کالاقتراب من الخمر للإراقة. وقال في القنية رامزاً لمجد الأئمة: وقد اختلف في نجاسة الكلب والذي صح عندي من الروايات في النوادر والآمالي نجس العين عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة ليس بنجس العين ا هـ . ومشى عليه ابن وهبان في منظومته وذكره في عقد الفوائد شرحها، وذكر الناطفي عن محمد إذا صلى على جلد كلب أو ذئب قد ذبح جازت صلاته، ولا يخفى أن هذه الرواية تفيد طهارة عينه عند محمد فيجوز أن يكون عن محمد روايتان ا هـ . وقال القاضي الاسبيجابي : وإما الكلب يحتمل الذكاة والدباغة في ظاهر الرواية خلافاً لما روى إلى كمال عدم قابلية الطهارة في الخنزير والتأخير في أمثال هذه المواضع يفيد التعظيم كما في قوله تعالى لهدمت صوامع وبيع وصلوات ومساجد يذكر ﴾ [الحج : ٤٠] والمصنف قدم الآدمي نظراً إلى كرامته. وذكر في عن أبي يوسف أن الخنزير إذا ذبح يطهر جلده بالدباغ والله تعالى أعلم. الخلاصة وهو الحسن ا هـ . فإذا علمت هذا فاعلم أن الجلد لا يطهر بالدباغ على القول بنجاسته ويطهر به على القول بطهارته ، وإذا وقع في بئر واستخرج حياً تنجس الماء كله مطلقاً على القول بنجاسته كما لو وقع الخنزير، وعلى القول بطهارته لا يتنجس إلا إذا وصل فمه الماء وإذا ذكي لا يطهر جلده ولا لحمه على القول بالنجاسة كالخنزير ويطهر على القول بالطهارة. وإذا صلى وهو حامل جرواً صغيراً لا تصح صلاته على القول بنجاسته مطلقاً وتصح على القول بطهارته. وإما مطلقاً أو بكونه مشدود الفم كما قدمناه عن البدائع. وتقييده بكونه جرواً صغيراً يظهر أن في الكبير لا تصح . مطلقاً لما أنه وإن لم يكن نجس العين فهو متنجس لأن مأواه النجاسات. وقد يقال ينبغي أن لا تصح صلاة من حمل جرواً صغيراً اتفاقاً، أما على القول بنجاسة عينه فظاهر، وأما على القول بطهارة عينه فلأن لحمة نجس بدليل أنهم اتفقوا على أن سؤره نجس لما أنه مختلط بلعابه ولعابه متولد من لحمه وهو نجس ولهذا قال في التنجيس : نجاسة السؤر دليل نجاسة اللحم . وقال العلامة في فتح القدير : نجاسة سؤره لا تستلزم نجاسة عينه بل تستلزم نجاسة لحمه المتولد منه اللعاب ا هـ . وسبب نجاسة لحمه اختلاط الدم المسفوح بأجزائه حالة الحياة مع حرمة أكله كما سنوضحه في بيان الاسآر إن شاء الله تعالى . وبهذا التقرير يندفع ما قد. إشكالاً يتوهم أن يقال كيف يكون سؤره نجساً على القول بطهارة عينه؟ فإن هذه غفلة عظيمة عن فهم كلامهم فإن قولهم بطهارة عينه لا يستلزم طهارة كل جزء منه ، ولهذا علل في البدائع لنجاسة سؤر الكلب وسائر السباع بأن سؤر هذه الحيوانات متحلب من لحومها ولحومها نجسة وقد قالوا إن حرمة الشيء إذا لم تكن للكرامة كحرمة الآدمي ولا لفساد الغذاء كالذباب والتراب ولا للخبث طبعاً كالضفدع والسلحفاة، ولا للمجاورة كالماء النجس كانت علامة النجاسة أي نجاسة اللحم فثبت بهذا أنه لا خلاف في نجاسة لحمه عندنا وإنما الخلاف في نجاسة عينه فظهر بهذا أن الكلب طاهر العين بمعنى طهارة عظمه وشعره وعصبه وما لا يؤكل منه لا بمعنى طهارة لحمه، لكن قد أجاب في المحيط قال : وإن كان فمه مشدوداً بحيث لا يصل لعابه إلى ثوبه جاز لأن ظاهر كل حيوان طاهر ولا يتنجس إلا بالموت ونجاسة باطنه في معدنه فلا يظهر حكمها كنجاسة باطن . المصلي. وفي شرح منية المصلي : لا يخفى أن هذا على القول بطهارة عينه، وأما على القول بأنه نجس العين فلا لظهور أن الصلاة لا تصح الحامله مطلقاً كما في حق حامل الخنزير. وإذا دخل الماء فانتقض فأصاب ثوب إنسان أفسده ولو أصابه ماء المطر لم يفسد لأن في الوجه الاول الماء أصاب الجلد وجلده نجس، وفي الوجه الثاني أصاب شعره وشعره طاهر. كذا ذكر الولوالجي وغيره. ولا يخفى أن هذا على القول بنجاسة عينه يستفاد منه أن الشعر طاهر قوله : (وتقييده بكونه جرواً صغير الخ قال في النهر : بل قيدوا به لوقوع التصوير بكونه في
Book of Purification. Selling by tanning. And he said in the chapter on impurity: The hide of a dog is purified by tanning according to us, contrary to al-Hasan and al-Shafi'i, because its essence is impure according to them, but we say: Benefit from it is permissible by choice; if its essence were impure, benefit from it would not be permitted. And this is explicit in contradicting the first. And he also mentioned in the Book of Hunting in the issue of the dog in the reasoning: 'And by this it becomes clear that it is not impure in essence.' And he mentioned in al-Idah the difference in transmission on it. In Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam: As for the dog's hide, there are two transmissions from our companions: in one transmission it becomes pure by tanning, and in another it does not become pure, and this is the apparent in the madhhab. And he mentioned in al-Bada'i that there is a difference among the shaykhs: whoever said it is impure in essence made it like the pig, and whoever made it pure in essence made it like other animals except the pig. And the correct is that it is not impure in essence, and similarly he corrected it in another place, and said: It is the closer of the two opinions to correctness. Therefore our shaykhs said concerning one who prays with a puppy in his sleeve, that his prayer is valid, and al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani restricted the permissibility to the mouth being tied. Thus al-Hidayah corrected the purity of its essence, and its commentators followed him like al-Atqani, al-Kaki, al-Sighnaqi. And Qadi Khan chose in al-Fatawa the impurity of its essence and derived branches from it. So the conclusion is that the correction has differed on it, and what is required by the general import of the texts like al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, and al-Kanz is the purity of its essence, and nothing that necessitates its impurity contradicts it, so the correctness of its non-impurity is due. Do you not see that benefit is derived from it for guarding and hunting? And it is explicitly stated in 'Uqud al-Fawa'id, commentary on the versification of Ibn Wahban, that the fatwa is on the purity of its essence. As for what was argued in al-Mabsut from the saying of Muhammad: 'The dead is not more impure than the dog and pig,' it was said in Ghayat al-Bayan: We do not concede that impurity of essence is established for the dog by this amount of speech. Whoever claims that must provide evidence, and no text has come from Muhammad regarding impurity of essence. And his objection that benefit does not necessitate purity of essence, for manure is used for kindling and strengthening agriculture despite its impurity, was answered in al-Nihaya etc. that this benefit is by consumption and is permissible for impure essence, like approaching wine for pouring out. And he said in al-Quniya, alluding to Majd al-A'imma: 'The impurity of the dog has been differed upon, and what is correct to me from the transmissions in al-Nawadir and al-Amali is that it is impure in essence according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Abu Hanifa it is not impure in essence.' End. And Ibn Wahban followed this in his versification and mentioned it in 'Uqud al-Fawa'id its commentary. And al-Natafi mentioned from Muhammad: If one prays on the hide of a dog or wolf that has been slaughtered, his prayer is valid. And it is not hidden that this transmission indicates the purity of its essence according to Muhammad, so it is possible that there are two transmissions from Muhammad. End. And al-Qadi al-Asbijabi said: 'As for the dog, it admits slaughter and tanning in the apparent transmission, contrary to what was transmitted...' to the extent of complete absence of capacity for purity in the pig, and delay in these places indicates veneration, as in His saying: 'Would have demolished monasteries, churches, synagogues, and mosques' (Quran 22:40). And the author prioritized the human due to his dignity. And he mentioned from Abu Yusuf that the pig, if slaughtered, its hide is purified by tanning. And Allah knows best. The summary: And it is al-Hasan. End. So when you know this, then know that the hide is not purified by tanning according to the opinion of its impurity, and it is purified by it according to the opinion of its purity. And if it falls into a well and is taken out alive, the water becomes wholly impurely absolutely according to the opinion of its impurity, like if a pig had fallen; and according to the opinion of its purity, it becomes impure only if its mouth reaches the water. And if it is slaughtered, its hide and meat are not purified according to the opinion of impurity, like the pig; and they are purified according to the opinion of purity. And if one prays while carrying a small puppy, his prayer is not valid according to the opinion of its impurity absolutely, and it is valid according to the opinion of its purity, either absolutely or with the condition that its mouth is tied, as we mentioned from al-Bada'i. And its restriction to a small puppy indicates that in a large dog the prayer is not valid absolutely, because even if it is not impure in essence, it is filthy (mutanajjis) since its abode is impurities. And it may be said that the prayer of one carrying a small puppy should not be valid by agreement: as for the opinion of its essential impurity, it is obvious; as for the opinion of its essential purity, because its flesh is impure, as evidenced by their agreement that its leftover water (su'r) is impure because it mixes with its saliva, and its saliva is generated from its flesh, which is impure. Hence it was said in al-Tanjis: 'The impurity of the leftover water is evidence of the impurity of the flesh.' And the scholar in Fath al-Qadir said: 'The impurity of its leftover water does not necessitate the impurity of its essence, but rather necessitates the impurity of its flesh from which the saliva is generated.' End. And the cause of impurity of its flesh is the mixture of flowing blood in its parts during life along with the prohibition of eating it, as we will clarify in the discussion of leftover water (as'ar) if Allah wills. And by this explanation is repelled what may be an imagined problem: how can its leftover water be impure according to the opinion of its essential purity? For this is a great negligence in understanding their words, because their statement of its essential purity does not necessitate the purity of every part of it. Hence in al-Bada'i the impurity of the leftover water of the dog and all beasts of prey is explained by saying that the leftover water of these animals is exuded from their flesh, and their flesh is impure. And they have said: If the prohibition of a thing is not for honor (like the human), nor for corruption of food (like flies and soil), nor for natural foulness (like frog and turtle), nor for adjacency (like impure water), then it is a sign of impurity, i.e., impurity of the flesh. Thus it is established that there is no dispute on the impurity of its flesh among us; the dispute is only on the impurity of its essence. So it becomes clear that the dog is pure in essence in the sense of the purity of its bone, hair, sinew, and those parts not eaten, not in the sense of purity of its flesh. However, an answer was given in al-Muhit: If its mouth is tied so that its saliva does not reach his garment, it is permissible, because the external of every animal is pure and only becomes impure by death, and the impurity of its interior in its place of origin does not manifest its ruling like the impurity of the interior of the one praying. And in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: It is not hidden that this is according to the opinion of its essential purity; but on the opinion that it is impure in essence, then no, because it is obvious that the prayer of its carrier is not valid absolutely, as in the case of the carrier of a pig. And if water enters and then spurts and hits someone's garment, it spoils it; but if rainwater hits it, it does not spoil it, because in the first case the water hit the skin and its skin is impure, while in the second case it hit its hair and its hair is pure. Thus mentioned al-Walwali and others. And it is not hidden that this, according to the opinion of its essential impurity, benefits that the hair is pure. His saying: (and its restriction to a small puppy...) He said in al-Nahr: Rather they restricted it because the scenario is of it being in...

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addresses a major intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the dog is impure in its essence (najis al-'ayn) or not. The author begins by referencing earlier discussions on tanning (dabgh). He notes that in Bab al-Hadath, the hide of a dog is purified by tanning according to the Hanafi school, opposing al-Hasan al-Basri and al-Shafi'i, who consider the dog's essence impure. The Hanafi reasoning is that if the dog were impure in essence, benefiting from it (e.g., use as guard or hunter) would not be permitted; since it is permitted, the essence must be pure. However, there is internal disagreement. The author cites from al-Mabsut that there are two transmissions from Hanafi scholars: one that tanning purifies the hide, and another that it does not, the latter being the apparent position (al-zahir min al-madhhab). In al-Bada'i, the difference is attributed to whether one analogizes the dog to the pig (impure) or to other animals (pure). The author states that the correct view is that it is not impure in essence, citing al-Hidayah and its commentators. Qadi Khan, however, chose impurity in his Fatawa. The author then argues that the general import of the canonical matns (al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Kanz) supports purity, and no counter-evidence necessitates impurity. He addresses objections, such as the use of manure (sirgin) which is impure but still used for kindling; the answer is that such use is by consumption (istihlak), permissible even for impure substances, analogous to pouring out wine. The passage then reports a transmission from al-Nawadir and al-Amali that the dog is impure in essence according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, while Abu Hanifa holds it pure. Ibn Wahban follows this, and al-Natafi reports a transmission from Muhammad that prayer on a slaughtered dog's hide is valid, indicating purity. The author then systematically explains the practical differences between the two positions: (1) Tanning: invalid on the impurity view, valid on the purity view. (2) Falling into a well: water becomes wholly impure on impurity view; only if mouth touches water on purity view. (3) Slaughter: hide and meat remain impure on impurity view, become pure on purity view (though meat remains haram). (4) Carrying a puppy in prayer: invalid on impurity view; valid on purity view, but only if the puppy's mouth is tied (to avoid saliva). The author clarifies that even on the purity view, the dog's flesh is impure because its saliva (and hence leftover water, su'r) is impure; this does not contradict essential purity, as essential purity refers to bone, hair, and non-edible parts. The commentary concludes with a note that if water splashes from a dog's wet body onto a garment, it spoils it (because the skin is impure), but rainwater hitting the hair does not spoil because the hair is pure. This entire discussion illustrates the nuanced methodology of Hanafi fiqh: reliance on the apparent meaning of transmitted texts, weighing of evidence (tarjih), and recognition of valid ikhtilaf within the school.

Key Terms
نجس العين (najis al-'ayn): Impure in its very essence, as opposed to being impure due to something external. The dog's entire body is considered impure.
دباغ (dabgh): The process of tanning animal hides to purify them. According to most Hanafis, tanning purifies the hide of any animal except the pig (and dog according to some).
سؤر (su'r): Leftover water after an animal drinks. The su'r of the dog is considered impure by all Hanafis, even those who hold the dog's essence pure, because it mixes with saliva from impure flesh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical implication of the view that the dog is impure in essence for a person praying while carrying a small puppy?
A) The prayer is valid unconditionally.
B) The prayer is valid only if the puppy's mouth is tied.
C) The prayer is not valid.
D) The prayer is valid only if the puppy is not wet.

Key Takeaway
The dog's essence (bone, hair) is pure according to the preferred Hanafi view, but its flesh and saliva are impure; this distinction governs practical rulings on tanning, water purity, and prayer validity.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
The Two Views on Dog's Impurity and Their Application
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dog's impurity with practical applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi views on the dog's impurity and apply each view to practical scenarios of taharah.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, the dog is pure in essence but its flesh and saliva are impure — a crucial distinction from the pig.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq delves into a foundational intra-Hanafi dispute: is the dog impure in its very essence (najis al-ayn) like the pig, or is it pure in its skin, hair, and bones while its flesh and saliva are impure? The answer determines rulings on tanning, prayer, water contamination, and more. The author presents both views, weighs the evidence, and establishes the mufta bihi (operative ruling).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing views on the dog's essence.
One view holds the dog is najis al-ayn (impure in essence), like the pig. The other holds it is tahir al-ayn (pure in essence) but its flesh and saliva are impure. State each view clearly.
The opposing view is attributed to some narrations from Abu Yusuf and others.
2
Locate the key evidence for each view.
The main evidence is the impurity of the dog's leftover (su'r). On the impurity view, this indicates impurity of the whole body. On the purity view, it only indicates impurity of the flesh. Also, the principle that prohibition not due to honor, spoilage, vileness, or adjacency indicates impurity of flesh.
The author of al-Tanjis states: 'The impurity of the leftover indicates the impurity of the flesh.'
3
Apply each view to the specific scenarios: tanning, well, prayer, shaking, biting.
Work through each scenario in the passage. For each, state the ruling on the impurity view versus the purity view. For example, tanning: on the impurity view, skin remains impure; on the purity view, tanning purifies the skin.
Pay attention to the restriction of 'small puppy' and 'mouth tied' in the prayer scenario.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) for each scenario.
Identify the practical difference in daily life. For instance, if a dog falls into a well, on the impurity view all water is impure; on the purity view, only the water touching the mouth is impure. This affects whether the well water can be used.
The thamarah al-khilaf is key to understanding why this dispute matters.
5
Recognize the tarjih (preference) and identify the mufta bihi.
The author indicates that the view of tahir al-ayn is the chosen view (al-mukhtar). Cite the authorities: al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Muhit, and others. Conclude that the mufta bihi is that the dog is pure in essence but its flesh and saliva are impure.
The opposing view is based on rare transmissions (nawadir) and is not relied upon for fatwa.

خلاف في نجاسة لحمه عندنا وإنما الخلاف في نجاسة عينه فظهر بهذا أن الكلب طاهر العين بمعنى طهارة عظمه وشعره وعصبه وما لا يؤكل منه لا بمعنى طهارة لحمه، لكن قد أجاب في المحيط قال : وإن كان فمه مشدوداً بحيث لا يصل لعابه إلى ثوبه جاز لأن ظاهر كل حيوان طاهر ولا يتنجس إلا بالموت ونجاسة باطنه في معدنه فلا يظهر حكمها كنجاسة باطن المصلي. وفي شرح منية المصلي : لا يخفى أن هذا على القول بطهارة عينه، وأما على القول بأنه نجس العين فلا لظهور أن الصلاة لا تصح الحامله مطلقاً كما في حق حامل الخنزير. وإذا دخل الماء فانتقض فأصاب ثوب إنسان أفسده ولو أصابه ماء المطر لم يفسد لأن في الوجه الاول الماء أصاب الجلد وجلده نجس، وفي الوجه الثاني أصاب شعره وشعره طاهر. كذا ذكر الولوالجي وغيره. ولا يخفى أن هذا على القول بنجاسة عينه يستفاد منه أن الشعر طاهر قوله : (وتقييده بكونه جرواً صغيراً الخ قال في النهر : بل قيدوا به لوقوع التصوير بكونه في على القول بنجاسة عينه لما ذكر في السراج الوهاج أن جلد الكلب نجس وشعره طاهر هو المختار ويتفرع عليه ذكر الفرع الذي ذكرناه، أما على القول بالطهارة إذا انتفض فأصاب ثوباً لا سواء أصاب شعره أو جلده ينجسه مطلقاً، للقول بنجاسة عينه فقال : من جعله نجس العين استدل بما ذكر في العيون عن أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى أن الكلب إذا وقع في الماء ثم خرج منه إلى آخر ما ذكرناه من التفصيل عن الولوالجي. ويدل عليه أيضاً أن صاحب التنجيس ذكر هذا الذي ذكرناه مع التفصيل من جملة مسائل ثم قال بعدها وهذا المسائل تشير إلى نجاسة عينه. ويدل عليه أيضاً ما ذكره في فتح القدير في آخر باب الأنجاس من مسائل شتى بما لفظه وما ذكره في الفتاوى من التنجس من وضع رجله موضع رجل كلب في الثلج أو الطين ونظائر هذه مبني على رواية نجاسة عين الكلب وليست بالمختارة ا هـ . فقوله ونظائر هذه أراد به مثل المسألة التي ذكرناها عن الولوالجي كما لا يخفى لكن ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه أن هذه المسألة مفرعة على القول بنجاسة عينه وعلل للنجاسة في مسألة ما إذا أصاب الماء جلده بتعليل آخر وهو أن مأواه النجاسات، فاستفيد منه أن الماء أصاب جلده وانتفض فأصاب الثوب نجسه أيضاً على القول بطهارة عينه لأنه لما كان مأواه النجاسات صار جلده متنجساً. وعلم مما قررناه أنه لا يدخل في قول من قال بنجاسة عين الكلب الشعر بخلاف قولهم بنجاسة عين الخنزير فإنه يدخل فيه شعره أيضاً، فإذا انتفض الخنزير فأصاب ثوباً نجسه مطلقاً . سواء أصاب الماء جلده أو شعره . كما صرح به في السراج الوهاج. وقال الولوالجي أيضاً : الكلب إذا أخذ عضو إنسان أو ثوبه إن أخذ في . الغضب لا يتنجس لأنه يأخذه بالأسنان ولا رطوبة فيها، وإن أخذه في حالة المزاج يتنجس لأنه يأخذه الأسنان والشفتين وشفتاه رطبة فيتنجس ا هـ . وكذا ذكر غيره. في القنية رامز اللوبري : عضه الكلب ولا يرى بللاً لا بأس به يعني لا يجب غسله، ولا يخفى أن ما في القنية إنما ينظر إلى وجود المقتضى للنجاسة وهو الريق سواء كان ملاعباً أو غضباناً . وهو الفقه . وقد صرح في الملتقط بأنه لا يتنجس ما لم ير البلل، سواء كان راضياً أو غضباناً . وفي الصيرفية هو المختار، وكذا في التتارخانية وواقعات الناطفي وغيرهما كذا في عقد الفوائد . حالة وفي خزانة الفتاوى وعلامة الابتلال أن لو أخذه بيده تبتل يده. ولا يخفى أن هذه المسألة على القولين؛ أما على القول بالنجاسة فظاهر، وأما على القول بطهارة عينه فلأن لعابه نجس لتولده من لحم نجس كما قدمناه وفي التنجيس: امرأة صلت وفي عنقها قلادة فيها كمه قوله : (وما لا يؤكل منه أي ما لا يمكن أكله احترازاً عن لحمه فإنه قابل للأكل. قوله : (لكن قد أجاب في المحيط) أي أجاب عما قدمه من قوله وقد يقال ينبغي الخ قال في النهر : ويدل عليه ما نقله في مسائل الآبار من أنه لو وقع في البئر وأخرج حياً لا ينجس الماء على القول بطهارة عينه ما
Book of Purity. This is al-Hasan, etc. So when you know this, know that the skin is not purified by tanning according to the view of its impurity, and it is purified by it according to the view of its purity. And if it falls into a well and is taken out alive, all the water becomes impugn absolutely according to the view of its impurity, as if a pig had fallen; and according to the view of its purity, it does not become impure unless its mouth touches the water. And if it is slaughtered (dhabiha), its skin and meat are not purified according to the view of impurity, like a pig; and they are purified according to the view of purity. And if one prays while carrying a small puppy, his prayer is not valid according to the view of its impurity absolutely, and it is valid according to the view of its purity. And either absolutely or with its mouth tied shut as we have mentioned from al-Bada'i'. And its restriction to a small puppy makes it clear that for a large dog it is absolutely invalid, because even if it is not impure in essence, it is still mutanajjis since its lair is impurities. And it may be said that the prayer of one carrying a small puppy should be invalid by agreement: as for the view of its essence being impure, it is obvious; as for the view of its essence being pure, because its flesh is impure, evidenced by their agreement that its leftover (su'r) is impure because it is mixed with its saliva, and its saliva is generated from its flesh which is impure. Hence it is stated in al-Tanjis: 'The impurity of the leftover indicates the impurity of the flesh.' And Allama in Fath al-Qadir said: 'The impurity of its leftover does not necessitate the impurity of its essence, but rather necessitates the impurity of its flesh from which the saliva is generated.' And the cause of the impurity of its flesh is the mixture of spilled blood with its parts during life, along with the prohibition of eating it, as we will clarify in the discussion of leftovers, God willing. By this exposition, the possible misgiving is repelled: how can its leftover be impure according to the view of its essence being pure? For this is a great negligence in understanding their words, because their saying 'its essence is pure' does not necessitate the purity of every part of it. Hence, in al-Bada'i' the impurity of the leftover of the dog and other predators is reasoned by the fact that the leftover of these animals is exuded from their flesh, and their flesh is impure. And they said: if the prohibition of a thing is not due to honor like the prohibition of a human, nor for spoiling food like flies and dust, nor for natural vileness like frog and turtle, nor for adjacency like impure water, then it is a sign of impurity—i.e., impurity of the flesh. Thus it is established that there is no dispute among us regarding the impurity of its flesh; rather the dispute is about the impurity of its essence. Hence it appears that the dog is pure in essence in the sense of the purity of its bones, hair, nerves, and what is not eaten from it, not in the sense of the purity of its flesh. However, al-Muhit gave a response: if its mouth is tied such that its saliva does not reach his garment, it is permissible, because the apparent of every animal is pure and does not become impure except by death, and the impurity of its interior in its essence does not manifest its ruling, like the impurity of the interior of the praying person. In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: it is clear that this is according to the view of its essence being pure; as for the view of its essence being impure, it is invalid because it is obvious that prayer is not valid while carrying it absolutely, as in the case of carrying a pig. And if water enters [the dog's fur] and it shakes itself, so water splashes on a person's garment, it spoils it; but if rainwater splashes on it, it does not spoil it because in the first case the water touched the skin and its skin is impure, and in the second case it touched its hair and its hair is pure. Thus mentioned al-Walwaliji and others. And it is clear that according to the view of its essence being impure, it can be understood that hair is pure. His statement: 'And its restriction to a small puppy...' al-Nahr said: Rather they restricted it because the scenario is that it is in a state... According to the view of its essence being impure, because it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that the dog's skin is impure and its hair is pure—this is the chosen view. And upon this branch the rulings we have mentioned. As for the view of purity, if it shakes and water hits a garment, there is no difference whether it hits its hair or its skin—it makes it impure absolutely, for those who hold it impure in essence. He said: Whoever considers it impure in essence adduced evidence from what is mentioned in al-Uyun from Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, that when a dog falls into water and then comes out, up to the end of the detail we mentioned from al-Walwaliji. Also evidence from the author of al-Tanjis, who mentioned this with detail among his issues and then said: 'These issues indicate its essence being impure.' Also evidence from Fath al-Qadir at the end of the chapter on impurities, where it states: 'What is mentioned in al-Fatawa about impurity from placing one's foot where a dog's foot was in snow or mud, and similar instances, are based on the transmission of the dog's essence being impure, and it is not the chosen view.' So his statement 'and similar instances' refers to the issue we mentioned from al-Walwaliji. But Qadikhan in his Fatawa stated that this issue is derived from the view of its essence being impure, and gave another reason for impurity in the case where water touches its skin: namely, that its lair is impurities. So it is understood from this that the water touched its skin and it shook, so the garment is also impure according to the view of its essence being pure, because since its lair is impurities, its skin becomes mutanajjis. And from what we have established, it is known that hair is not included in the statement of those who say the dog's essence is impure, contrary to their saying the pig's essence is impure, for that includes its hair as well. So if a pig shakes and water hits a garment, it makes it impure absolutely, whether the water touched its skin or its hair, as stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Al-Walwaliji also said: If a dog takes hold of a human's limb or garment, if it takes in anger it does not become impure because it grabs with teeth and there is no moisture; if it takes in a casual state it becomes impure because it grabs with teeth and lips, and its lips are wet, so it becomes impure. And others mentioned similarly. In al-Qunyah of Ramz al-Lubury: If a dog bites and no wetness is seen, there is no harm, meaning it is not necessary to wash it. And it is clear that what is in al-Qunyah looks to the presence of the effective cause of impurity, which is saliva, whether playful or angry. That is the fiqh. And al-Multaqat explicitly states that it does not become impure unless wetness is seen, whether the dog is pleased or angry. And in al-Sayrafiyyah, that is the chosen view, likewise in al-Tatarkhaniyyah and Waqi'at al-Natifi and others, as in 'Uqd al-Fawa'id. In Khizanat al-Fatawa: the sign of wetness is that if it took it with its hand, its hand would become wet. And it is clear that this issue is according to both views: as for the view of impurity, it is obvious; as for the view of the essence being pure, because its saliva is impure, generated from impure flesh as we have mentioned. And in al-Tanjis: a woman prayed while having a necklace with... His statement: 'and what is not eaten from it' means what cannot be eaten, as a precaution against its flesh, for it is capable of being eaten. His statement: 'but in al-Muhit there is a response' means a response to what he had previously said: 'And it may be said that it should be invalid...' al-Nahr said: what supports it is what is transmitted in Masa'il al-Abar: that if it falls into a well and is taken out alive, it does not make the water impure according to the view of its essence being pure.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq delves into a fundamental intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the impurity (najasa) of the dog. The central question is whether the dog's entire body is considered impure in essence (najis al-ayn) or whether only its flesh and saliva are impure while its skin, hair, and bones remain pure (tahir al-ayn). The author methodically applies these two positions to several practical scenarios, showing how the ruling changes accordingly. The scenarios include: (1) tanning of dog skin, (2) a dog falling into a well, (3) carrying a small puppy during prayer, (4) water from a wet dog splashing on clothes, (5) a dog biting a person. The correct Hanafi position, as per the mufta bihi, is that the dog's essence is pure, but its flesh and saliva are impure. Its hair and skin are pure. This is supported by the evidence from the leftover (su'r) of the dog being impure, which points only to the impurity of the flesh, not the whole body. The author also clarifies that the pig is different: its entire essence, including hair, is impure.

Key Terms
نجس العين (najis al-ayn): The condition of being impure in essence; the entire body of the animal is considered impure by itself.
طاهر العين (tahir al-ayn): The condition of being pure in essence; the animal's skin, hair, and bones are pure, though its flesh may be impure.
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water or liquid that remains after an animal drinks from a vessel; also refers to the animal's saliva.
متنجس (mutanajjis): Something that becomes impure due to contact with an impure substance, as opposed to being impure in essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what is the ruling on the dog's hair?
A) It is impure like the pig's hair.
B) It is pure, but the skin is impure.
C) It is pure.
D) It is impure only if wet.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the dog's pure essence and impure flesh, yielding practical differences from the pig, which is fully impure.

The Dog's Hair and Skin: Distinguishing Impurity in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on dog impurity with intra-Hanafi dispute and practical application to water splashing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the impurity of a dog's skin and hair, explain the evidence, and apply the distinction to cases of water splashing.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, a dog's hair is pure, but its skin is impure; water that touches only the hair does not render a garment impure.

This lesson explores a key distinction in Hanafi taharah: the dog is not considered essentially impure (najis al-ayn) like the pig. Instead, only its skin and saliva are impure, while its hair remains pure. This ruling has practical implications when water splashes from a dog onto a person's garment, as the source passage from Bahru al-Ra'iq explains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Position on Dog Impurity
Distinguish between the rulings on the dog's skin and hair. The chosen view (mukhtar) is that the skin is impure (najis) and the hair is pure (tahir).
This is the mufta bihi in the school.
2
Recognize the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Note that some Hanafi scholars, including a narration from Abu Yusuf, considered the entire dog impure. The preferred view distinguishes skin and hair.
The dispute is based on whether the dog is considered najis al-ayn.
3
Understand the Proof for the Chosen View
The passage cites authorities like al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Bada'i' as evidence that the hair is not included in the impurity. The dog is not considered essentially impure.
The proof is based on the school's reliance on later consensus and preferred narrations.
4
Apply the Ruling to Water Splashing
If a dog shakes water that hits only its hair, the garment remains pure. If the water hits the dog's skin, the garment becomes impure and must be washed.
This is the practical branch (far') derived from the ruling.
5
Contrast with the Pig
The pig is considered najis al-ayn, so its hair is also impure. If a pig shakes and water hits its hair or skin, the garment becomes impure.
This contrast highlights the unique Hanafi position on the dog.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على القول بنجاسة عينه لما ذكر في السراج الوهاج أن جلد الكلب نجس وشعره طاهر هو المختار ويتفرع عليه ذكر الفرع الذي ذكرناه، أما على القول بالطهارة إذا انتفض فأصاب ثوباً لا سواء أصاب شعره أو جلده ويدل عليه أن صاحب البدائع ذكر هذا الفرع شاهداً ينجسه مطلقاً، للقول بنجاسة عينه فقال : من جعله نجس العين استدل بما ذكر في العيون عن أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى أن الكلب إذا وقع في الماء ثم خرج منه إلى آخر ما ذكرناه من التفصيل عن الولوالجي. ويدل عليه أيضاً أن صاحب التنجيس ذكر هذا الذي ذكرناه مع التفصيل من جملة مسائل ثم قال بعدها وهذا مسائل تشير إلى نجاسة عينه. ويدل عليه أيضاً ما ذكره في فتح القدير في آخر باب الأنجاس من مسائل شتى بما لفظه وما ذكره في الفتاوى من التنجس من وضع رجله موضع رجل كلب في الثلج أو الطين ونظائر هذه مبني على رواية نجاسة عين الكلب وليست بالمختارة ا هـ . فقوله ونظائر هذه أراد به مثل المسألة التي ذكرناها عن الولوالجي كما لا يخفى لكن ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه أن هذه المسألة مفرعة على القول بنجاسة عينه وعلل للنجاسة في مسألة ما إذا أصاب الماء جلده بتعليل آخر وهو أن مأواه النجاسات، فاستفيد منه أن الماء أصاب جلده وانتفض فأصاب الثوب نجسه أيضاً على القول بطهارة عينه لأنه لما كان مأواه النجاسات صار جلده متنجساً. وعلم مما قررناه أنه لا يدخل في قول من قال بنجاسة عين الكلب الشعر بخلاف قولهم بنجاسة عين الخنزير فإنه يدخل فيه شعره أيضاً، فإذا انتفض الخنزير فأصاب ثوباً نجسه مطلقاً . سواء أصاب الماء جلده أو شعره . كما صرح به في السراج الوهاج.
According to the opinion of its [the dog's] being essentially impure, as mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: the dog's skin is impure and its hair is pure, which is the chosen view, and derived from it is the mention of the branch we mentioned. As for the opinion of purity, if it shakes and water hits a garment, it is not the same whether it hits its hair or its skin. This is supported by the fact that the author of al-Bada'i' mentioned this branch as a witness for the absolute impurity [of dog] according to the opinion of its essential impurity, and he said: 'He who makes it essentially impure argues by what is mentioned in al-'Uyun from Abu Yusuf that if a dog falls into water and then comes out...' Up to the end of the detail we mentioned from al-Walwaliji. It is also supported by the fact that the author of al-Tanjis mentioned what we mentioned with detail among the matters and then said after it: 'These matters indicate its essential impurity.' It is also supported by what is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir at the end of the chapter on impurities from miscellaneous matters: 'What is mentioned in al-Fatawa about impurity due to placing one's foot in the place of a dog's foot in snow or mud and similar cases are based on the narration of the essential impurity of the dog, and it is not the chosen view.' So his statement 'and similar cases' refers to the case we mentioned from al-Walwaliji, as is not hidden. However, Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatawa that this case is derived from the opinion of its essential impurity, and he explained impurity in the case of water hit its skin with another explanation: that its habitat is impurities. So it is understood that if water hits its skin and it shakes and hits a garment, it also makes it impure according to the opinion of its essential purity, because since its habitat is impurities, its skin becomes impure. And from what we have established, it is known that the hair does not enter into the statement of those who say the dog is essentially impure, contrary to their statement about the essential impurity of the pig, for its hair enters into it as well. So if a pig shakes and hits a garment, it makes it impure absolutely, whether water hits its skin or its hair, as stated explicitly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on the impurity of a dog's body, specifically distinguishing between skin and hair. The author states that according to the chosen view (al-mukhtar), the dog's skin is impure (najis) while its hair is pure (tahir). This is a key point in Hanafi fiqh: the dog is not considered entirely impure (najis al-ayn) according to the preferred opinion; rather, only its skin and saliva are impure. The passage then addresses the scenario where a dog shakes itself after getting wet, and drops of water splatter onto a person's garment. The ruling depends on whether the water touched the dog's skin or hair. If the water touched the skin, it becomes impure and will make the garment impure. If it only touched the hair, it remains pure according to the chosen view. The author supports this with citations from earlier Hanafi authorities like al-Bada'i', al-Tanjis, Fath al-Qadir, and Qadikhan, showing that the majority of the school holds this position. He also contrasts the dog with the pig, which is considered entirely impure (including its hair). Thus, if a pig shakes and water hits its hair, the garment becomes impure.

Key Terms
نجس العين (najis al-ayn): A thing whose very substance is considered impure, like pig; for dog, it is debated.
مختار (mukhtar): The chosen or preferred opinion within the Hanafi school.
انتقض (intaqada): To shake off water (like a dog shaking itself).
متنجس (mutanajjis): A pure thing that becomes impure through contact with an impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what happens if a dog shakes and water from its hair only splashes onto a person's garment?
A) The garment becomes impure and must be washed three times.
B) The garment becomes impure only if the water was on the dog's skin first.
C) The garment remains pure because the dog's hair is pure.
D) The garment becomes impure regardless because the dog is impure.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the dog's hair is pure; only its skin and saliva convey impurity, so water splashing from the hair does not require purification.

Dog's Bite: Condition of Wetness for Impurity
Determining when a dog's bite requires washing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a dog's bite transfers impurity and explain why visible wetness is the decisive factor.

Core Idea
A dog's bite transfers impurity only when visible wetness from saliva is present.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi ruling on impurity from a dog's bite. The key factor is not the dog's emotional state (anger vs play) but the presence of wetness. Understanding this distinction avoids unnecessary washing and ensures proper purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? A dog's bite to a person's limb or garment. Does it cause impurity? The ruling depends on the presence of wetness.
2
Understand the cause of impurity
The cause (muqtadi) is the dog's saliva (riq), which is impure because it is generated from impure flesh. Saliva is the actual impure substance.
3
Apply the condition of wetness
The condition for impurity to transfer is that the saliva must be visible (ball). If no wetness is seen, the area remains pure. This is the relied-upon view (mukhtar).
The dog's state (playful/angry) is an indicator but not decisive; the decisive factor is visual wetness.
4
Note the authoritative position
Many Hanafi authorities (al-Multaqat, al-Sayrafiyyah, al-Tatar Khaniyyah) confirm that the ruling hinges on visible wetness, regardless of the dog's mood or the underlying debate on the dog's essence.
This ruling is consistent even on the opinion that the dog's body is pure, because its saliva is impure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الولوالجي أيضاً : الكلب إذا أخذ عضو إنسان أو ثوبه إن أخذ في الغضب لا يتنجس لأنه يأخذه بالأسنان ولا رطوبة فيها، وإن أخذه في حالة المزاج يتنجس لأنه يأخذه الأسنان والشفتين وشفتاه رطبة فيتنجس ا هـ . وكذا ذكر غيره. في القنية رامز اللوبري : عضه الكلب ولا يرى بللاً لا بأس به يعني لا يجب غسله، ولا يخفى أن ما في القنية إنما ينظر إلى وجود المقتضى للنجاسة وهو الريق سواء كان ملاعباً أو غضباناً . وهو الفقه . وقد صرح في الملتقط بأنه لا يتنجس ما لم ير البلل، سواء كان راضياً أو غضباناً . وفي الصيرفية هو المختار، وكذا في التتارخانية وواقعات الناطفي وغيرهما كذا في عقد الفوائد . وفي خزانة الفتاوى وعلامة الابتلال أن لو أخذه بيده تبتل يده. ولا يخفى أن هذه المسألة على القولين؛ أما على القول بالنجاسة فظاهر، وأما على القول بطهارة عينه فلأن لعابه نجس لتولده من لحم نجس كما قدمناه
Al-Walwaliji also said: If a dog seizes a limb of a person or his garment, if it seizes in anger, it does not become impure because it seizes with its teeth and there is no moisture in them. If it seizes in a playful state, it becomes impure because it seizes with teeth and lips, and its lips are moist, so it becomes impure. Similarly mentioned by others. In al-Qunyah: 'Ramiz al-Lubari: If a dog bites him and no wetness is seen, there is no harm, meaning it is not obligatory to wash it.' It is not hidden that what is in al-Qunyah looks only at the existence of the cause of impurity, which is saliva, whether the dog is playing or angry, and that is the fiqh. It is stated explicitly in al-Multaqat that it does not become impure unless wetness is seen, whether the dog is pleased or angry. In al-Sayrafiyyah, that is the chosen view, and likewise in al-Tatar Khaniyyah, Waqi'at al-Natifi, and others, as in 'Uqud al-Fawa'id. In Khazanat al-Fatawa: the sign of wetting is that if he takes it [the dog] with his hand, his hand becomes wet. It is not hidden that this matter [the ruling] depends on the two opinions: as for the opinion of impurity (of the dog's essence), it is apparent; as for the opinion of its essential purity, because its saliva is impure due to being generated from impure flesh, as we have previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of impurity (najasa) resulting from a dog's bite. The key factor is the presence of moisture (wetness) from the dog's mouth. If the dog bites in anger, it typically uses only its teeth, which are dry, so no impurity transfers. If it bites in play (mizaj), it uses both teeth and lips, and the lips are moist, so impurity transfers. However, the standard is to look for visible wetness (ball) on the bitten area. If no wetness is seen, the area remains pure and washing is not required. This is the relied-upon view (mukhtar) according to many Hanafi authorities like al-Sayrafiyyah and al-Tatar Khaniyyah. The passage also ties this back to the earlier dispute: even on the opinion that the dog's essence is pure, its saliva is impure because it comes from impure flesh. So the ruling remains the same regardless of the underlying view on the dog's essence.

Key Terms
بلل (ball): Wetness or moisture, specifically from dog's saliva.
ريق (riq): Saliva of the dog, which is considered impure because it is generated from impure flesh.
مزاج (mizaj): Playful state of the dog, as opposed to anger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary condition for a dog's bite to transfer impurity?
A) The dog must be angry.
B) The dog must be playful.
C) Visible wetness from saliva must be present.
D) The bite must draw blood.

Key Takeaway
A dog's bite transmits impurity only when visible saliva wetness is present; otherwise, the affected part remains pure.

Purity of Dog's Teeth and Effect of Slaughter
Ruling on the purity of dog's teeth based on the effect of slaughter (tadhkiya)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the purity of dog's teeth and explain the proof from tadhkiya.

Core Idea
Dog's teeth are pure because tadhkiya applies, making the bone pure.

This lesson examines the purity of dog's teeth, a practical issue for daily worship. The ruling hinges on whether the dog is considered pure in essence or subject to ritual slaughter. By analyzing the source text, you will understand the proof from tadhkiya and the intra-Hanafi difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific case described? A woman prays while wearing a necklace containing a dog's tooth. The ruling: her prayer is valid (complete) because the tooth is pure.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the general principle: 'Everything that is subject to tadhkiya, its bone is not impure.' This implies that if an animal can be slaughtered Islamically, its bones (including teeth) become pure.
The proof is not a direct Quranic verse but a derived principle from the effect of tadhkiya.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The link: the dog is an animal that can be slaughtered (tadhkiya applies). Therefore, its bones are pure. This applies to lions and foxes as well.
This is contrasted with humans and pigs, which are not subject to tadhkiya.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some early Hanafis (including Abu Hanifa) held that the dog is essentially impure (najis al-ayn), so tadhkiya has no effect, making its teeth impure.
This view is considered weak (marjuh) in the later school.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that dog's teeth are pure, upheld by later authorities like the authors of al-Tanjis and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Thus, in practice, wearing a dog's tooth in prayer is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التنجيس: امرأة صلت وفي عنقها قلادة فيها سن كلب أو أسد أو ثعلب فصلاتها تامة لأنه يقع عليها الذكاة وكل ما يقع عليه الذكاة فعظمه لا يكون نجساً بخلاف الآدمي والخنزير ا.هـ. وكذا ذكر الولوالجي. وذكر في السراج الوهاج معزياً إلى الذخيرة أسنان الكلب طاهرة وأسنان الآدمي نجسة لأن الكلب يقع عليه الذكاة بخلاف الخنزير والآدمي ا.هـ. ولا يخفى أن هذا كله على القول بطهارة عينه لأنه علله بكونه يطهر بالذكاة، وأما على القول بنجاسة عينه فلا تعمل فيه الذكاة فتكون أسنانه نجسة كالخنزير وسيأتي الكلام على أسنان الآدمي إن شاء الله تعالى قريباً.
And in al-Tanjis: 'A woman prayed while around her neck was a necklace containing the tooth of a dog, a lion, or a fox; her prayer is complete because they are subject to ritual slaughter (tadhkiya), and everything that is subject to tadhkiya, its bone is not impure, contrary to the human and the pig.' Similarly al-Walwaliji mentioned. And it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, citing al-Dhakhirah: 'The teeth of a dog are pure and the teeth of a human are impure because the dog is subject to tadhkiya, unlike the pig and the human.' It is not hidden that all of this is according to the opinion of the dog's essential purity (taharat al-ayn), because he explains that it is purified by tadhkiya. As for the opinion of its essential impurity (najis al-ayn), tadhkiya does not work on it, so its teeth would be impure like the pig. And the discussion on human teeth will come soon, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage addresses the purity of dog's teeth, which is a practical issue (e.g., wearing a necklace with a dog's tooth while praying). According to the view that the dog is essentially pure (tahir al-ayn), its teeth are pure because the dog is an animal that can be slaughtered (tadhkiya applies to it). The principle is: any animal that is subject to Islamic slaughter, its bones (including teeth) are pure. This is contrasted with the pig (which cannot be slaughtered) and the human (who is not subject to tadhkiya). Therefore, on this view, prayer is valid with such a necklace. However, on the opposing view that the dog is essentially impure (najis al-ayn), tadhkiya has no effect, and the teeth would be impure like those of a pig. The author notes that the discussion on human teeth will follow later.

Key Terms
ذكاة (tadhkiyya): Ritual slaughter according to Islamic law, which purifies the meat and makes the animal's body parts pure.
سن (sinn): Tooth; in this context, the tooth of an animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, why are a dog's teeth considered pure?
A) Because the dog's saliva is pure.
B) Because the dog is subject to ritual slaughter (tadhkiya).
C) Because the dog's teeth are not flesh.
D) Because the dog is always pure in essence.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that dog's teeth are pure because tadhkiya applies; the minority view of impurity is marjuh.

Dog Eating from a Vessel: Impurity and Purification by Drying
Ruling on a vessel from which a dog eats three times, and purification by drying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a vessel from which a dog eats three times and explain why it is not purified by drying, distinguishing it from grass.

Core Idea
A vessel from which a dog eats three times is not purified by drying; drying only purifies items connected to the earth by istihsan.

This lesson examines a specific taharah ruling: the impurity of a vessel from which a dog has eaten three times. We will see why the Hanafi school rejects the analogy to grass, which is purified by drying, and understand the principle of istihsan that underlies this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The dog eats from a vessel three times; the vessel becomes impure. Note the condition of three separate instances.
The number three is significant in Hanafi fiqh for dog's contamination.
2
Recognize the proposed analogy
Some might argue that drying could purify the vessel, by analogy to grass (kala') which becomes pure by drying.
Grass is a standard example of something connected to earth.
3
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal
The text rejects this analogy, stating that grass is purified by drying only by istihsan because it is connected to the earth; the vessel lacks this connection.
Istihsan is a juristic preference over qiyas.
4
Understand the basis of istihsan
The purification of grass is a special concession based on a hadith, not a general rule.
This hadith-based exception is confined to earth-connected items.
5
Apply the distinction
Thus, a vessel from which a dog eats requires washing (number of washes not specified here), not drying.
The general rule for dog's saliva is washing three times, one with earth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا أكل من شيء ثلاثاً ويؤكل كذا في المبتغى بالغين المعجمة وينبغي أن يكون هذا بالاتفاق كما لا يخفى، ولا يقال ينبغي أن يطهر بالجفاف قياساً على الكلأ إذا تنجس فإنه يطهر به كما في الخلاصة والخانية لأنا نقول : الطهارة في الكلأ بالجفاف حصلت استحساناً بالأثر لكونه في معنى الأرض لاتصاله بها وما نحن فيه ليس كذلك.
As for if it [the dog] eats from something three times, and it is eaten, such is in al-Mubtagha with the dotted ghain, and it should be that this [ruling] is agreed upon, as is not hidden. And one should not say that it should become purified by drying, by analogy to green grass (kala'), which if it becomes impure, it is purified by it [drying], as in al-Khulasa and al-Khaniyya. For we say: purification of grass by drying occurred by istihsan due to the trace [hadith] because it is in the meaning of earth due to its connection to it, and our case here is not like that.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage addresses the impurity of a vessel from which a dog eats repeatedly (specifically three times). The ruling is that such a vessel becomes impure and is not purified by simply drying it. The author rejects an analogy with grass (kala') that becomes pure by drying because grass is connected to the earth, which has purifying properties by istihsan. The dog's eating from a vessel does not share that connection, so the drying method does not apply. The passage implies that the vessel must be washed, although the number of washes is not specified here. The phrase 'يؤكل' might indicate that the food itself is considered eaten (i.e., the dog consumes it), but the focus is on the vessel.

Key Terms
كلأ (kala'): Green grass or herbage; considered in the meaning of earth for purification by drying.
جفاف (jifaf): Drying; a method of purification for certain things connected to earth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the vessel is made of metal.
D) Because the dog only eats once.

Key Takeaway
A vessel from which a dog eats three times is not purified by drying; drying is only valid for items connected to the earth by istihsan.

Eating Tanned Hide of a Dead Animal: The Hanafi Prohibition
Debate on eating tanned dead animal hide

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating tanned hide of a dead halal animal and explain the evidence (Quran 5:3 and hadith of Maymunah) that distinguishes purification for use from permissibility for consumption.

Core Idea
Tanning purifies the hide for use, not for eating; the dead animal prohibition covers all parts.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a nuanced point: does tanning transform the hide of a dead animal into something permissible to eat, if the animal is of a halal species? Some scholars argued yes, because tanning makes the hide pure like that of a properly slaughtered animal. However, the correct Hanafi position, supported by clear textual evidence, maintains that the hide remains prohibited for consumption. The key is to distinguish between functional purification (taharah) and legal permissibility (hilla).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the legal question being debated? Determine whether the hide of a dead animal (maytah) that belongs to a halal species becomes permissible to eat after being tanned.
The disagreement is not about using the hide for clothing, but about eating it.
2
State the opposing view and its basis
Some scholars hold that after tanning the hide becomes pure like the hide of a slaughtered animal, thus permissible to eat. They reason that tanning removes the impurity of death entirely.
This view is not attributed to a specific school in the text, but it is a position that exists.
3
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school (as presented here) holds that eating the tanned hide is not permissible. The proof is the general Quranic prohibition of dead animals (5:3) and the hadith of Maymunah's sheep where the Prophet distinguished between eating (forbidden) and using the tanned hide (permitted).
The hadith explicitly says 'What is forbidden from a dead animal is eating it' while commanding them to tan and benefit.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing view
The Hanafi response is that the opposing argument conflates two different categories: tanning removes najasah (ritual impurity) for external use, but it does not change the inherent haram status of dead meat. The Quranic verse covers all parts of the dead animal, and the hadith reinforces the separation.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that a person following the permissive view could eat tanned hide; the Hanafi prohibits it.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a sheep that died of natural causes. Its hide is tanned professionally. According to the Hanafi school, the hide may be used as a prayer mat or bag, but eating it is haram. If someone were to eat it, the act would be sinful.
This ruling is consistent with the principle that dead animals are entirely off-limits for consumption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن في قول المصنف في أصل المسأله «دبغ» إشارة إلى يستوي أن يكون الدايخ مسلماً أو كافراً أو صبياً أو مجنوناً أو امرأة إذا حصل به مقصود الدباغ، فإن دبغه الكافر وغلب على الظن أنهم يدبغون بالسمن النجس فإنه يغسل كذا في السراج الوهاج وفيه مسألة جلد الميتة بعد الدباغ هل يجوز أكله إذا كان جلد حيوان مأكول اللحم قال بعضهم : نعم لأنه طاهر كجلد الشاة المذكاة. وقال بعضهم : لا يجوز أكله وهو الصحيح لقوله تعالى حرمت عليكم الميتة ﴾ [المائدة : ٣] وهذا جزء منها. وقال عليه السلام في شاة ميمونة رضي الله تعالى عنها : إنما يحرم من الميتة أكلها مع أمره لهم بالدباغ والانتفاع. وأما لم يصل فمه الماء وهو الأصح .اهـ. قوله : (كجلد الشاة المذكاة قال الرملي أقول: يعني في الحل، وسواء فيها قبل الدباغ وبعده كنحو أكل تراب لا يضر فحل جلد المذكاة قبل الدباغ وبعده حيث كان
Then know that the author's statement in the original issue 'tanning' (dabgh) indicates that it is equal whether the one who tans is a Muslim, a disbeliever, a child, an insane person, or a woman, if the purpose of tanning is achieved. If a disbeliever tans it and there is a strong presumption that they tan with impure fat, then it is washed (afterwards), as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And in it [the text] is the issue: The hide of a dead animal after tanning: is it permissible to eat it if it is the hide of an animal whose meat is edible? Some said: Yes, because it is pure like the hide of a slaughtered sheep. Some said: It is not permissible to eat it, and that is the correct view, because Allah says: 'Forbidden to you are dead animals' [5:3], and this [hide] is a part of it. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said regarding the sheep of Maymunah, may Allah be pleased with her: 'What is forbidden from a dead animal is eating it,' while commanding them to tan and benefit [from the hide]. As for [the case where] its mouth does not reach the water, that is the most correct. His statement: 'like the hide of a slaughtered sheep' — al-Ramli says: I say it means in permissibility (hull), and it is the same whether before tanning or after, like eating soil that does no harm, so the hide of a slaughtered animal is permissible before and after tanning, wherever it is.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on the hide of a dead animal (maytah) after tanning. The opening clarifies that tanning is effective regardless of who performs it (Muslim, disbeliever, etc.) provided the tanning process is properly done. If the tanner is a disbeliever and there is presumption that impure substances were used, the hide must be washed. The core dispute: Can the tanned hide of a dead animal belonging to a species that is halal to eat (e.g., sheep) be eaten after tanning? One opinion says yes because tanning purifies it completely, making it like the hide of a properly slaughtered animal. The correct opinion (as per the author) says no, because the prohibition on dead animals includes all parts, and tanning only purifies for external use (like clothing), not for consumption. The Quranic verse forbidding dead animals is cited, and a hadith about the sheep of Maymunah is invoked: the Prophet allowed the use of the tanned skin but forbade eating it. The author also mentions that if the animal's mouth did not reach water (perhaps a condition for some ruling?), but the text is cut off. The final note from al-Ramli clarifies that the hide of a slaughtered animal is permissible to use and eat before and after tanning, as it is not dead meat.

Key Terms
دبغ (dabgh): Tanning process of hides, which purifies the skin for external use but does not make it edible.
ميتة (maytah): A dead animal that was not properly slaughtered; its consumption is haram even after tanning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tanning purifies dead animal hide for use, not for consumption; the Quran and hadith clearly prohibit eating any part of a dead animal.

Purification of Hides Through Tanning: Hadith Dispute and Hanafi Position
Defending Hanafi view against hadith criticism and inter-madhhab objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hide purification by tanning, identify the contested hadith of Ibn Ukaym, and evaluate the Hanafi response to Shafi'i and Maliki objections.

Core Idea
Tanning purifies any hide with any agent that removes stench and decay, even sun or earth.

The purification of animal hides through tanning is a practical issue with clear differences between the madhhabs. The Hanafi school takes the broadest view: any substance that effectively cleanses the hide renders it pure, including simple methods like sunning and dusting. This lesson examines the hadith evidence and scholarly disputes, particularly focusing on the contested hadith of Ibn Ukaym and the responses to the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on hide purification
The Hanafi school rules that tanning (dabgh) purifies the hide of a dead animal (maytah) and that any agent achieving the purpose—sun, earth, salt, or chemical tanning—suffices. The hide becomes pure (tahir) and can be used for liquids or dry goods.
This is based on the general meaning of dabgh and the authentic hadith of Sawdah.
2
Analyze the opposing hadith (Ibn Ukaym) and its weaknesses
The opposition cites the hadith of Abdullah ibn Ukaym suggesting the Prophet prohibited using skins after tanning. The Hanafi response shows the hadith has multiple weaknesses: disruption (idtirab) in its text (different durations: month, 40 days, 3 days), unknown narrators, and questions about Ibn Ukaym's Companionship.
Even if deemed hasan by al-Tirmidhi, it is outweighed by stronger authentic hadiths.
3
Examine the Hanafi response to the Maliki objection
Malik reportedly argued against tanning purification. The author refutes this by citing the authentic hadith of Sawdah: the Companions tanned a hide and used it for brewing liquid. This demonstrates the hide was pure, as they used it for liquid (which would be contaminated if impure).
The hadith of Sawdah is from Bukhari and is clear proof.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i restricts valid tanning agents to water and qaraz (oak galls) based on a hadith of Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi response argues that the term dabgh includes sunning and dusting; the hadith does not necessitate exclusivity. The purpose of removing stench and decay is achieved by any effective agent.
The Hanafi position is more comprehensive and aligns with the linguistic and rational meaning of dabgh.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: Hanafis allow using tanned hides even for liquids (like storing water or milk), while Shafi'is may restrict to dry use unless tanned with specific agents. Also, Hanafis permit using hides from any animal (excluding pig and dog if considered inherently impure) after tanning.
This directly impacts daily life, e.g., using leather products, prayer mats, or water containers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالتاء فوق - عن عبد الرحمن أنه انطلق هو وناس إلى عبد الله بن عكيم قال : فدخلوا ووقفت على الباب فخرجوا إلي فأخبروني أن عبد الله بن عكيم أخبرهم أنه عليه السلام كتب إلى جهينة الحديث. ففي هذا أنه سمع من الداخلين وهم مجهولون، وأما في المتن ففي رواية بشهر، وفي أخرى بأربعين يوماً، وفي أخرى بثلاثة أيام هذا مع الاختلاف في صحبة ابن عكيم ثم كيف كان لا يوازي حديث ابن عباس الصحيح في جهة من جهات الترجيح؟ ثم لو كان لم يكن قطعياً في معارضته لأن الإهاب اسم لغير المدبوغ وبعده يسمى . شناً وأديماً وما رواه الطبراني في الأوسط من لفظ هذا الحديث هكذا كنت رخصت لكم في جلود الميتة فلا تنتفعوا من الميتة بجld ولا عصب في سنده فضالة بن مفضل مضعف. والحق أن حديث ابن عكيم ظاهر في النسخ لولا الاضطراب المذكور فإن من المعلوم أن أحداً لا ينتفع بجلد الميتة قبل الدباغ لأنه حينئذ مستقذر فلا يتعلق النهي به ظاهراً كذا في فتح القدير وفيه كلام من وجوه الأول أنه ذكر أن الترمذي حسنه وقد قدمناه أيضاً والحسن لا اضطراب فيه . الثاني أن قوله مع الاختلاف في صحبة ابن عكيم لا يقدح في حجيته لأنه على تقدير كونه ليس صحابياً يكون الحديث مرسلاً وأنتم تعملون به الثالث أن قوله الحق أن حديث ابن عكيم ظاهر في النسخ الخ أخذاً من قول الحازمي كما نقله الزيلعي المخرج عنه أنه قال : وطريق الإنصاف أن حديث بن عكيم ظاهر الدلالة في النسخ ولكنه كثير الاضطراب غير مسلم لأن أخبارنا مطلقة فيجوز أن يكون بعضها قبل وفاته بدون المدة المذكورة في حديث ابن عكيم على الاختلاف فيها، وبهذا صرح النووي في شرح المهذب. ويمكن الجواب عن الأول بما ذكره النووي أن الترمذي إنما حسنه بناء على اجتهاده وقد بين هو وغيره وجه ضعفه، وعن الثاني بأن هذا أعني كونه مرسلاً صالح لأن يجاب به على مذهب من يرى العمل بالمرسل لا أنه جواب عن حديث ابن عكيم على مقتضى مذهبنا. وأما الجواب عن احتجاج مالك فهو مخالف للنصوص الصحيحة التي قدمناها فإنها عامة في طهارة الظاهر والباطن، وأصرح من ذلك ما رواه البخاري من حديث سودة قالت: ماتت لنا شاة فدبغنا مسكها وهو جلدها فما زلنا ننتبذ فيه حتى صار شناً . وهو حديث صحيح فإنه استعمل في مائع وهم لا يجيزونه وإن كانوا يجيزون شرب الماء منه لأن الماء لا يتنجس عندهم إلا بالتغير . وأما الجواب عن احتجاج الشافعي؛ إن قلنا بأن الكلب ليس بنجس العين وأن جلده يطهر بالدباغ فهو عموم الأحاديث الصحيحة المتقدمة فإنه يدخل في عمومها الكلب لأن «أي» في الحديث نكرة وصفت بصفة عامة فتعم كما عرف في الأصول، وأما الخنزير فإنما خرج عن العموم لعارض ذكرناه، ولقد أنصف النووي حيث قال في شرح المهذب : واحتج أصحابنا بأحاديث لا دلالة فيها فتركتها لأني التزمت في خطبة الكتاب الإعراض عن الدلائل الواهية ا هـ . وإن قلنا إن الكلب كالخنزير فلا يحتاج إلى الجواب وقد قدمنا أن الدباغ جائز بكل ما يمنع النتن والفساد ولو تراباً أو ملحاً. وقال الشافعي لا يجوز بالشمس والتراب والملح لما رواه الدارقطني والبيهقي من حديث ابن عباس في شاة ميمونة قال : إنما حرم أكلها أو ليس في الماء والقرظ ما يطهرها؟ وهو حديث حسن ذكره النووي في شرح المهذب، ورواه أبو داود والنسائي في سننهما بمعناه عن ميمونة قال : يطهرها الماء والقرظ. ولنا ما تقدم من الأحاديث الصحيحة. فإن اسم الدباغ يتناول ما يقع بالتشميس والتتريب فلا يقيد بشيء ولأن المقصود يحصل به فلا معنى لاشتراط غيره وليس الحديث الذي استدل به الشافعي مما يقتضي الاختصاص بل المراد به ما في معناه بالإجماع، ولا يختص بما ذكر في الحديث.
With the letter 'ta' above - from Abd al-Rahman that he went with some people to Abdullah ibn Ukaym said: they entered and I stood at the door, then they came out to me and informed me that Abdullah ibn Ukaym told them that the Prophet (peace be upon him) wrote to Juhaynah the hadith. In this, he heard from those who entered while they were unknown. As for the text, in one narration it is a month, in another forty days, in another three days, this in addition to the difference regarding the Companionship of Ibn Ukaym. Then how could it match the authentic hadith of Ibn Abbas in any aspect of preponderance? Moreover, if it were, it would not be decisive in opposing it because 'ihab' is the name for untanned hide, and after tanning it is called 'shann' and 'adim'. What al-Tabarani narrated in al-Awsat from the wording of this hadith: 'I had permitted you to use the skins of dead animals, so do not benefit from dead animals' skin or sinew' – in its chain is Fudalah ibn Mufaddal, who is weak. The truth is that the hadith of Ibn Ukaym apparently indicates abrogation were it not for the mentioned disruption, for it is known that no one benefits from the skin of a dead animal before tanning because then it is repulsive, so the prohibition does not apply to it apparently. This is in Fath al-Qadir. There is discussion from several aspects: first, he mentioned that al-Tirmidhi deemed it hasan, and we have already mentioned it, and the hasan has no disruption. Second, his statement about the disagreement regarding the Companionship of Ibn Ukaym does not impugn its authority, because if he is not a Companion, the hadith becomes mursal, and you act upon it. Third, his statement 'the truth is that the hadith of Ibn Ukaym is apparently abrogative' is taken from al-Hazimi as al-Zayla'i narrated from him. He said: the way of fairness is that the hadith of Ibn Ukaym is apparently indicative of abrogation, but it has much disruption and is not accepted because our reports are absolute; it is possible that some of them occurred before his death without the mentioned period in the hadith of Ibn Ukaym, given the difference about it. Al-Nawawi stated this in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab. The first point can be answered by what al-Nawawi mentioned: al-Tirmidhi only deemed it hasan based on his ijtihad, and he and others have explained its weakness. As for the second, this being mursal is suitable to answer according to the school that accepts mursal, but it is not an answer to the hadith of Ibn Ukaym according to our school. As for the answer to Malik's argument, it contradicts the authentic texts we presented, which are general in purifying the apparent and inner. Clearer than that is what al-Bukhari narrated from the hadith of Sawdah: 'A sheep of ours died, so we tanned its skin – that is its hide – and we continued to brew in it until it became a shann.' This is an authentic hadith, for it was used for liquid, but they do not permit that, although they permit drinking water from it because water does not become impure according to them except by change. As for the answer to al-Shafi'i's argument: If we say that the dog is not inherently impure and its hide is purified by tanning, then the general authentic hadiths mentioned earlier include the dog because 'any' in the hadith is an indefinite noun described by a general adjective, so it generalizes as known in usul. As for the pig, it is excluded from the generality due to an impediment we mentioned. Indeed al-Nawawi was fair when he said in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab: 'Our companions argued with hadiths that have no indication, so I left them because I committed in the book's preface to disregard weak evidences.' If we say the dog is like the pig, then no answer is needed, and we have already stated that tanning is permissible with anything that prevents stench and decay, even earth or salt. Al-Shafi'i said it is not permissible with sun, earth, and salt, because of what al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi narrated from the hadith of Ibn Abbas regarding the sheep of Maymunah: 'He only prohibited eating it; is there not in water and qaraz what purifies it?' This is a hasan hadith mentioned by al-Nawawi in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, and Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i narrated it in their Sunan with similar meaning from Maymunah: 'Water and qaraz purify it.' We have the authentic hadiths mentioned earlier. The name 'dabgh' includes what occurs by sunning and dusting, so it is not restricted to anything, and because the purpose is achieved by it, there is no point in stipulating something else. The hadith used by al-Shafi'i does not necessitate exclusivity; rather, what is intended is something similar by consensus, and it is not specific to what is mentioned in the hadith.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute defending the Hanafi position on the purification of animal hides through tanning. The author begins by criticizing the hadith of Abdullah ibn Ukaym, which some opponents use to argue that tanning does not purify. He points out weaknesses in its chain and text, including contradictions in the reported duration and questions about Ibn Ukaym's Companionship. The hadith of Ibn Abbas that supports tanning is stronger. The author then addresses objections: first, that al-Tirmidhi deemed the hadith hasan – al-Nawawi explains this was his own ijtihad and others have shown its weakness. Second, even if mursal, it is not accepted in the Hanafi school. Third, the idea that it indicates abrogation is refuted because the earlier reports are absolute. The author then refutes Malik's argument by citing the hadith of Sawdah where tanned hide was used for liquid, proving purification. Against al-Shafi'i, who restricts tanning to water and qaraz, the Hanafi position is that any agent (sun, earth, salt) that removes stench and decay suffices. The hadiths cited by al-Shafi'i are general and not exclusive. The overall ruling: tanning purifies the hide, and it is permissible to use any agent that achieves the purpose.

Key Terms
دباغ (dabgh): The process of treating animal hide to remove stench and decay, making it pure; includes methods like tanning, sunning, and dusting.
إهاب (ihāb): Untanned hide; after tanning it is called shann or adim.
ميتة (maytah): A dead animal not slaughtered Islamically; its hide is impure before tanning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for a tanning agent (dabgh) according to the Hanafi school, as argued in this passage?
A) It must be water and qaraz (oak galls).
B) It must be earth or salt.
C) It must be something that removes stench and decay.
D) It must be a chemical tanning agent.

Key Takeaway
Tanning purifies any animal hide with any agent that removes stench and decay, a robust Hanafi position supported by authentic hadiths.
